                               '<p><b>Humans</b> (<i><b>Homo sapiens</b></i>) '
                               'or <b>modern humans</b> are the most common '
                               'and widespread <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Species">species</a> '
                               'of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Primate">primate</a>, '
                               'and the last surviving species of the genus '
                               '<i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo">Homo</a></i>. '
                               'They are <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hominidae">great '
                               'apes</a> characterized by their <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prehistory_of_nakedness_and_clothing#Evolution_of_hairlessness">hairlessness</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bipedality">bipedalism</a>, '
                               'and high <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_intelligence">intelligence</a>. '
                               'Humans have large <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_brain">brains</a>, '
                               'enabling more advanced <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive">cognitive</a> '
                               'skills that enable them to thrive and adapt in '
                               'varied environments, develop highly complex <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tool">tools</a>, '
                               'and form complex <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_structures">social '
                               'structures</a> and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civilization">civilizations</a>. '
                               'Humans are <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sociality">highly '
                               'social</a>, with individual humans tending to '
                               'belong to a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Level_of_analysis">multi-layered</a> '
                               'network of distinct <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_groups">social '
                               'groups</a> &ndash; from <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Families">families</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peer_groups">peer '
                               'groups</a> to <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corporations">corporations</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_(polity)">political '
                               'states</a>. As such, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_interaction">social '
                               'interactions</a> between humans have '
                               'established a wide variety of values, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norm_(sociology)">social '
                               'norms</a>, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Language">languages</a>, '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Traditions">traditions</a> '
                               '(collectively termed <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institutions">institutions</a>), '
                               'each of which bolsters human <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Society">society</a>. '
                               'Humans are also highly <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Curious">curious</a>: '
                               'the desire to understand and influence <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phenomenon">phenomena</a> '
                               "has motivated humanity's development of <a "
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science">science</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technology">technology</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophy">philosophy</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mythology">mythology</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion">religion</a>, '
                               'and other frameworks of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge">knowledge</a>; '
                               'humans also study themselves through such '
                               'domains as <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anthropology">anthropology</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_science">social '
                               'science</a>, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History">history</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psychology">psychology</a>, '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medicine">medicine</a>. '
                               'As of 2025, there are estimated to be <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_population">more '
                               'than 8 billion humans alive</a>.</p>\n'
                               '<p>For most of their history, humans were <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nomadic">nomadic</a> '
                               'hunter-gatherers. Humans began exhibiting <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Behavioral_modernity">behavioral '
                               'modernity</a> about 160,000&ndash;60,000 years '
                               'ago. The <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution">Neolithic '
                               'Revolution</a>, which began in <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southwest_Asia">Southwest '
                               'Asia</a> around 13,000 years ago (and '
                               'separately in a few other places), saw the '
                               'emergence of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agriculture">agriculture</a> '
                               'and permanent <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_settlement">human '
                               'settlement</a>; in turn, this led to the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cradle_of_civilization">development '
                               'of civilization</a> and kickstarted a period '
                               'of continuous (and ongoing) <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_growth">population '
                               'growth</a> and rapid <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technological_change">technological '
                               'change</a>. Since then, a number of '
                               'civilizations have risen and fallen, while a '
                               'number of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sociocultural_evolution">sociocultural</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_technology">technological</a> '
                               'developments have resulted in significant '
                               'changes to the human lifestyle.</p>\n'
                               '<p>Although some scientists equate the term '
                               '&quot;humans&quot; with all members of the '
                               'genus <i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo">Homo</a></i>, '
                               'in common usage it generally refers to <i>Homo '
                               'sapiens</i>, the only <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extant_taxon">extant</a> '
                               'member. All other members of the genus '
                               '<i>Homo</i>, which are now extinct, are known '
                               'as <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archaic_humans">archaic '
                               'humans</a>, and the term &quot;modern '
                               'human&quot; is used to distinguish <i>Homo '
                               'sapiens</i> from archaic humans. <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_modern_human">Anatomically '
                               'modern humans</a> emerged around 300,000 years '
                               'ago in Africa, evolving from <i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo_heidelbergensis">Homo '
                               'heidelbergensis</a></i> or a similar species. '
                               'Migrating <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recent_African_origin_of_modern_humans">out '
                               'of Africa</a>, they gradually replaced and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hybrid_(biology)">interbred</a> '
                               'with local populations of archaic humans. '
                               'Multiple hypotheses for the extinction of '
                               'archaic human species <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neanderthal_extinction">such '
                               'as Neanderthals</a> include competition, '
                               'violence, interbreeding with <i>Homo '
                               'sapiens</i>, or inability to adapt to climate '
                               'change. <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gene">Genes</a> '
                               'and the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environment_(biophysical)">environment</a> '
                               'influence human biological variation in '
                               'visible characteristics, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physiology">physiology</a>, '
                               'disease susceptibility, mental abilities, body '
                               'size, and life span. Though humans vary in '
                               'many traits (such as genetic predispositions '
                               'and physical features), humans are among the '
                               'least genetically diverse primates. Any two '
                               'humans are at least 99% genetically similar. '
                               'Humans are <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sex_differences_in_humans">sexually '
                               'dimorphic</a>: generally, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Man">males</a> '
                               'have greater body strength and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Woman">females</a> '
                               'have a higher <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Body_fat">body '
                               'fat</a> percentage. At <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puberty">puberty</a>, '
                               'humans develop <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secondary_sex_characteristic">secondary '
                               'sex characteristics</a>. Females are capable '
                               'of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pregnancy">pregnancy</a>, '
                               'usually between puberty, at around 12 years '
                               'old, and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Menopause">menopause</a>, '
                               'around the age of 50.</p>\n'
                               '<p>Humans are <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Omnivorous">omnivorous</a>, '
                               'capable of consuming a wide variety of plant '
                               'and animal material, and have <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_of_fire_by_early_humans">used '
                               'fire</a> and other forms of heat to prepare '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cooking">cook</a> '
                               'food since the time of <i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo_erectus">Homo '
                               'erectus</a></i>. Humans have had a dramatic <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_impact_on_the_environment">effect '
                               'on the environment</a>. They are <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apex_predator">apex '
                               'predators</a>, being rarely preyed upon by '
                               'other species.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> '
                               'Human <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_growth">population '
                               'growth</a>, industrialization, land '
                               'development, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Overconsumption">overconsumption</a> '
                               'and combustion of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fossil_fuels">fossil '
                               'fuels</a> have led to <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_destruction">environmental '
                               'destruction</a> and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pollution">pollution</a> '
                               'that significantly contributes to the ongoing '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocene_extinction">mass '
                               'extinction</a> of other forms of life.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> '
                               'Within the last century, humans have explored '
                               'challenging environments such as <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antarctica">Antarctica</a>, '
                               'the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deep_sea">deep '
                               'sea</a>, and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outer_space">outer '
                               'space</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Heim-1991-4">[4]</a></sup> '
                               'Human habitation within these hostile '
                               'environments is restrictive and expensive, '
                               'typically limited in duration, and restricted '
                               'to <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific">scientific</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military">military</a>, '
                               'or <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industry_(economics)">industrial</a> '
                               'expeditions.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Heim-1991-4">[4]</a></sup> '
                               'Humans have visited the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exploration_of_the_Moon">Moon</a> '
                               'and made their presence known on other <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celestial_bodies">celestial '
                               'bodies</a> through human-made <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robotic_spacecraft">robotic '
                               'spacecraft</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> '
                               'Since the early 20th century, there has been '
                               'continuous human presence in Antarctica '
                               'through <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Research_stations_in_Antarctica">research '
                               'stations</a> and, since 2000, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_presence_in_space">in '
                               'space</a> through habitation on the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Space_Station">International '
                               'Space Station</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> '
                               'Humans can survive for up to eight weeks '
                               'without <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Food">food</a> '
                               'and several days without <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water">water</a>. '
                               'Humans are generally <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diurnality">diurnal</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sleep">sleeping</a> '
                               'on average seven to nine hours per day. <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Childbirth">Childbirth</a> '
                               'is dangerous, with a high risk of '
                               'complications and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death">death</a>. '
                               'Often, both the mother and the father provide '
                               'care for their children, who are <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Altricial">helpless '
                               'at birth</a>.</p>\n'
                               '<h2>Etymology and definition</h2>\n'
                               '<p>Further information: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Names_for_the_human_species">Names '
                               'for the human species</a> and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_taxonomy">Human '
                               'taxonomy</a></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Carl_von_Linn%C3%A9,_1707-1778,_botanist,_professor_(Alexander_Roslin)_-_Nationalmuseum_-_15723.tif"><img '
                               'data-file-height="3655" data-file-width="3032" '
                               'src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Carl_von_Linn%C3%A9%2C_1707-1778%2C_botanist%2C_professor_%28Alexander_Roslin%29_-_Nationalmuseum_-_15723.tif/lossy-page1-340px-Carl_von_Linn%C3%A9%2C_1707-1778%2C_botanist%2C_professor_%28Alexander_Roslin%29_-_Nationalmuseum_-_15723.tif.jpg" '
                               'srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Carl_von_Linn%C3%A9%2C_1707-1778%2C_botanist%2C_professor_%28Alexander_Roslin%29_-_Nationalmuseum_-_15723.tif/lossy-page1-255px-Carl_von_Linn%C3%A9%2C_1707-1778%2C_botanist%2C_professor_%28Alexander_Roslin%29_-_Nationalmuseum_-_15723.tif.jpg '
                               '1.5x, '
                               '//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Carl_von_Linn%C3%A9%2C_1707-1778%2C_botanist%2C_professor_%28Alexander_Roslin%29_-_Nationalmuseum_-_15723.tif/lossy-page1-340px-Carl_von_Linn%C3%A9%2C_1707-1778%2C_botanist%2C_professor_%28Alexander_Roslin%29_-_Nationalmuseum_-_15723.tif.jpg '
                               '2x"></img></a><figcaption><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl_Linnaeus">Carl '
                               'Linnaeus</a> coined the name <i>Homo '
                               'sapiens</i></figcaption></figure>\n'
                               '<p>All modern humans are classified into the '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Species">species</a> '
                               '<i>Homo sapiens</i>, coined by <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl_Linnaeus">Carl '
                               'Linnaeus</a> in his 1735 work <i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Systema_Naturae">Systema '
                               'Naturae</a></i>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> '
                               'The <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Name_of_a_biological_genus">generic '
                               'name</a> <i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo">Homo</a></i> '
                               'is a learned 18th-century derivation from '
                               'Latin <i>homō</i>, which refers to humans of '
                               'either sex.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> '
                               'The word <i>human</i> can refer to all members '
                               'of the <i>Homo</i> genus.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Barras-2016-12">[12]</a></sup> '
                               "The name <i>Homo sapiens</i> means 'wise man' "
                               "or 'knowledgeable man'.<sup><a "
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> '
                               'There is disagreement if certain extinct '
                               'members of the genus, namely <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neanderthal">Neanderthals</a>, '
                               'should be included as a separate species of '
                               'humans or as a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subspecies">subspecies</a> '
                               'of <i>H. sapiens</i>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Barras-2016-12">[12]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p><i>Human</i> is a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loanword">loanword</a> '
                               'of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English">Middle '
                               'English</a> from <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French">Old '
                               'French</a> <i>humain</i>, ultimately from <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin">Latin</a> '
                               '<i>hūmānus</i>, the adjectival form of '
                               "<i>homō</i> ('man' &ndash; in the sense of "
                               'humanity).<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> '
                               'The native English term <i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Man_(word)">man</a></i> '
                               'can refer to the species generally (a synonym '
                               'for <i>humanity</i>) as well as to human '
                               'males. It may also refer to individuals of '
                               'either sex.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Despite the fact that the word '
                               '<i>animal</i> is colloquially used as an '
                               'antonym for <i>human</i>,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> '
                               'and contrary to a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_common_misconceptions#Biology">common '
                               'biological misconception</a>, humans are <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animal">animals</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> '
                               'The word <i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Person">person</a></i> '
                               'is often used interchangeably with '
                               '<i>human</i>, but philosophical debate exists '
                               'as to whether <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Personhood">personhood</a> '
                               'applies to all humans or all <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sentient_being">sentient '
                               'beings</a>, and further if a human can lose '
                               'personhood (such as by going into a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persistent_vegetative_state">persistent '
                               'vegetative state</a>).<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h2>Evolution</h2>\n'
                               '<p>Main article: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_evolution">Human '
                               'evolution</a></p>\n'
                               '<p>Humans are apes (<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hominoidea">superfamily '
                               'Hominoidea</a>).<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> '
                               'The <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lineage_(evolution)">lineage</a> '
                               'of apes that eventually gave rise to humans '
                               'first split from <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gibbon">gibbons</a> '
                               '(family Hylobatidae) and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orangutan">orangutans</a> '
                               '(genus <i>Pongo</i>), then <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gorilla">gorillas</a> '
                               '(genus <i>Gorilla</i>), and finally, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chimpanzee">chimpanzees</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bonobo">bonobos</a> '
                               '(genus <i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pan_(genus)">Pan</a></i>). '
                               'The last split, between the human and '
                               'chimpanzee&ndash;bonobo lineages, took place '
                               'around 8&ndash;4 million years ago, in the '
                               'late <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miocene">Miocene</a> '
                               'epoch.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> '
                               'During this split, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chromosome_2">chromosome '
                               '2</a> was formed from the joining of two other '
                               'chromosomes, leaving humans with only 23 pairs '
                               'of chromosomes, compared to 24 for the other '
                               'apes.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> '
                               'Following their split with chimpanzees and '
                               'bonobos, the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hominini">hominins</a> '
                               'diversified into many species and at least two '
                               'distinct genera. All but one of these lineages '
                               '&ndash; representing the genus <i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo">Homo</a></i> '
                               'and its sole extant species <i>Homo '
                               'sapiens</i> &ndash; are now extinct.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lucy_Skeleton.jpg"><img '
                               'data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1362" '
                               'src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Lucy_Skeleton.jpg/340px-Lucy_Skeleton.jpg" '
                               'srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Lucy_Skeleton.jpg/255px-Lucy_Skeleton.jpg '
                               '1.5x, '
                               '//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Lucy_Skeleton.jpg/340px-Lucy_Skeleton.jpg '
                               '2x"></img></a><figcaption>Reconstruction of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucy_(Australopithecus)">Lucy</a><i>,</i> '
                               'the first <i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australopithecus_afarensis">Australopithecus '
                               'afarensis</a></i> skeleton '
                               'found</figcaption></figure>\n'
                               '<p>The genus <i>Homo</i> evolved from <i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australopithecus">Australopithecus</a></i>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> '
                               'Though <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_fossils">fossils</a> '
                               'from the transition are scarce, the earliest '
                               'members of <i>Homo</i> share several key '
                               'traits with <i>Australopithecus</i>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Villmoare2015-27">[27]</a></sup> '
                               'The earliest record of <i>Homo</i> is the 2.8 '
                               'million-year-old specimen <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LD_350-1">LD '
                               '350-1</a> from <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, '
                               'and the earliest named species are <i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo_habilis">Homo '
                               'habilis</a></i> and <i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo_rudolfensis">Homo '
                               'rudolfensis</a></i> which evolved by 2.3 '
                               'million years ago.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Villmoare2015-27">[27]</a></sup> '
                               '<i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo_erectus">H. '
                               'erectus</a></i> (the African variant is '
                               'sometimes called <i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo_ergaster">H. '
                               'ergaster</a></i>) evolved 2 million years ago '
                               'and was the first <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archaic_human">archaic '
                               'human</a> species to leave Africa and disperse '
                               'across Eurasia.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> '
                               '<i>H. erectus</i> also was the first to evolve '
                               'a characteristically human <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Body_plan">body '
                               'plan</a>. <i>Homo sapiens</i> emerged in '
                               'Africa around 300,000 years ago from a species '
                               'commonly designated as either <i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo_heidelbergensis">H. '
                               'heidelbergensis</a></i> or <i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo_rhodesiensis">H. '
                               'rhodesiensis</a></i>, the descendants of <i>H. '
                               'erectus</i> that remained in Africa.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> '
                               '<i>H. sapiens</i> migrated out of the '
                               'continent, gradually replacing or '
                               'interbreeding with local populations of '
                               'archaic humans.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> '
                               'Humans began exhibiting <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Behavioral_modernity">behavioral '
                               'modernity</a> about 160,000&ndash;70,000 years '
                               'ago,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> '
                               'and possibly earlier.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> '
                               'This development was likely selected amidst <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_variability_and_change">natural '
                               'climate change</a> in <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Pleistocene">Middle</a> '
                               'to <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_Pleistocene">Late '
                               'Pleistocene</a> Africa.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>The <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recent_African_origin_of_modern_humans">&quot;out '
                               'of Africa&quot; migration</a> took place in at '
                               'least two waves, the first around 130,000 to '
                               '100,000 years ago, the second (<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Dispersal">Southern '
                               'Dispersal</a>) around 70,000 to 50,000 years '
                               'ago.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> '
                               '<i>H. sapiens</i> proceeded to colonize all '
                               'the continents and larger islands, arriving in '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasia">Eurasia</a> '
                               '125,000 years ago,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> '
                               'Australia around 65,000 years ago,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> '
                               'the Americas around 15,000 years ago, and '
                               'remote islands such as <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hawaiian_Islands">Hawaii</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Easter_Island">Easter '
                               'Island</a>, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madagascar">Madagascar</a>, '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Zealand">New '
                               'Zealand</a> in the years 300 to 1280 '
                               'CE.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Human evolution was not a simple linear or '
                               'branched progression but involved <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interbreeding_between_archaic_and_modern_humans">interbreeding '
                               'between related species</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-pmid21179161-43">[43]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> '
                               'Genomic research has shown that hybridization '
                               'between substantially diverged lineages was '
                               'common in human evolution.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DNA">DNA</a> '
                               'evidence suggests that several genes of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neanderthal">Neanderthal</a> '
                               'origin are present among all non '
                               'sub-Saharan-African populations, and '
                               'Neanderthals and other hominins, such as <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denisovan">Denisovans</a>, '
                               'may have contributed up to 6% of their <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genome">genome</a> '
                               'to present-day non sub-Saharan-African '
                               'humans.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-pmid21179161-43">[43]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Human evolution is characterized by a '
                               'number of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morphology_(biology)">morphological</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_development_(biology)">developmental</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_physiology">physiological</a>, '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_behavior">behavioral</a> '
                               'changes that have taken place since the split '
                               'between the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chimpanzee%E2%80%93human_last_common_ancestor">last '
                               'common ancestor of humans and chimpanzees</a>. '
                               'The most significant of these adaptations are '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prehistory_of_nakedness_and_clothing#Evolution_of_hairlessness">hairlessness</a>,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> '
                               'obligate bipedalism, increased brain size and '
                               'decreased <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_dimorphism">sexual '
                               'dimorphism</a> (<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neoteny">neoteny</a>). '
                               'The relationship between all these changes is '
                               'the subject of ongoing debate.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<table> <tbody><tr> <td><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hominoidea">Hominoidea</a> '
                               '(hominoids, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ape">apes</a>) '
                               '</td> <td rowspan="2"> <br> <table> '
                               '<tbody><tr>  <td></td> <td rowspan="2"> '
                               '<p>Hylobatidae (<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gibbon">gibbons</a>) '
                               '</p> </td></tr> <tr> <td> </td></tr> <tr> '
                               '<td>Hominidae (hominids, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_ape">great '
                               'apes</a>) </td> <td rowspan="2"> <br> <table> '
                               '<tbody><tr> <td><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ponginae">Ponginae</a> '
                               '</td> <td rowspan="2"> <br> <table> '
                               '<tbody><tr> <td>Pongo (<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orangutan">orangutans</a>) '

                               '</td> <td rowspan="2"> <br> <table> '

                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pan_troglodytes">Pan '
                               'troglodytes</a></i> </p> </td></tr> <tr> <td> '
                               '</td></tr> <tr>  <td></td> <td rowspan="2"> '
                               '<p><i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pan_paniscus">Pan '
                               'paniscus</a></i> </p> </td></tr> <tr> <td> '
