                               '<p>Early human settlements were dependent on '
                               'proximity to <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_resources">water</a> '
                               'and &ndash; depending on the lifestyle &ndash; '
                               'other <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_resource">natural '
                               'resources</a> used for <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subsistence">subsistence</a>, '
                               'such as populations of animal prey for <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunting">hunting</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arable_land">arable '
                               'land</a> for growing crops and grazing '
                               'livestock.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup> '
                               'Modern humans, however, have a great capacity '
                               'for altering their <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Habitat_(ecology)">habitats</a> '
                               'by means of technology, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irrigation">irrigation</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urban_planning">urban '
                               'planning</a>, construction, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deforestation">deforestation</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desertification">desertification</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup> '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_settlements">Human '
                               'settlements</a> continue to be <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulnerability">vulnerable</a> '
                               'to <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_disasters">natural '
                               'disasters</a>, especially those placed in '
                               'hazardous locations and with low quality of '
                               'construction.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup> '
                               'Grouping and deliberate habitat alteration is '
                               'often done with the goals of providing '
                               'protection, accumulating comforts or material '
                               'wealth, expanding the available food, '
                               'improving <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aesthetics">aesthetics</a>, '
                               'increasing knowledge or enhancing the exchange '
                               'of resources.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Humans are one of the most <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adaptation">adaptable</a> '
                               'species, despite having a low or narrow '
                               "tolerance for many of the earth's extreme "
                               'environments.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Piantadosi-2003-136">[134]</a></sup> '
                               'Currently the species is present in all eight '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biogeographical_realms">biogeographical '
                               'realms</a>, although their presence in the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antarctic_realm">Antarctic '
                               'realm</a> is very limited to <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Research_stations_in_Antarctica">research '
                               'stations</a> and annually there is a '
                               'population decline in the winter months of '
                               'this realm. Humans established nation-states '
                               'in the other seven realms, such as <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa">South '
                               'Africa</a>, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India">India</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia">Russia</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australia">Australia</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fiji">Fiji</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States">United '
                               'States</a> and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brazil">Brazil</a> '
                               '(each located in a different biogeographical '
                               'realm).</p>\n'
                               '<p>By using advanced tools and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clothing">clothing</a>, '
                               'humans have been able to extend their '
                               'tolerance to a wide variety of temperatures, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humidity">humidities</a>, '
                               'and altitudes.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Piantadosi-2003-136">[134]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup> '
                               'As a result, humans are a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosmopolitan_distribution">cosmopolitan</a> '
                               'species found in almost all regions of the '
                               'world, including <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_rainforest">tropical '
                               'rainforest</a>, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desert">arid '
                               'desert</a>, extremely cold <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arctic_region">arctic '
                               'regions</a>, and heavily polluted cities; in '
                               'comparison, most other species are confined to '
                               'a few geographical areas by their limited '
                               'adaptability.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-138">[136]</a></sup> '
                               'The <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_population">human '
                               'population</a> is not, however, uniformly '
                               'distributed on the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth">Earth</a>\'s '
                               'surface, because the population density varies '
                               'from one region to another, and large '
                               'stretches of surface are almost completely '
                               'uninhabited, like <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antarctica">Antarctica</a> '
                               'and vast swathes of the ocean.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Piantadosi-2003-136">[134]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup> '
                               'Most humans (61%) live in Asia; the remainder '
                               'live in the Americas (14%), Africa (14%), '
                               'Europe (11%), and Oceania (0.5%).<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Distribution-of-earths-mammals.png"><img '
                               'data-file-height="2360" data-file-width="2454" '
                               'src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Distribution-of-earths-mammals.png/660px-Distribution-of-earths-mammals.png" '
                               'srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Distribution-of-earths-mammals.png/495px-Distribution-of-earths-mammals.png '
                               '1.5x, '
                               '//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Distribution-of-earths-mammals.png/660px-Distribution-of-earths-mammals.png '
                               '2x"></img></a><figcaption> Humans and their '
                               'domesticated animals represent 96% of all '
                               'mammalian biomass on earth, whereas all wild '
                               'mammals represent only 4%.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bar-On-141">[139]</a></sup></figcaption></figure>\n'
                               '<p>Estimates of the population at the time '
                               'agriculture emerged in around 10,000 BC have '
                               'ranged between 1 million and 15 '
                               'million.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup> '
                               'Around 50&ndash;60 million people lived in the '
                               'combined eastern and western <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Empire">Roman '
                               'Empire</a> in the 4th century AD.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup> '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bubonic_plague">Bubonic '
                               'plagues</a>, first recorded in the 6th century '
                               'AD, reduced the population by 50%, with the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Death">Black '
                               'Death</a> killing 75&ndash;200 million people '
                               'in <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasia">Eurasia</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Africa">North '
                               'Africa</a> alone.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup> '
                               'Human population is believed to have reached '
                               'one billion in 1800. It has since then '
                               'increased exponentially, reaching two billion '
                               'in 1930 and three billion in 1960, four in '
                               '1975, five in 1987 and six billion in '
                               '1999.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup> '
                               'It passed seven billion in 2011<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup> '
                               'and passed eight billion in November '
                               '2022.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup> '
                               'It took over two million years of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prehistory">human '
                               'prehistory</a> and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_history">history</a> '
                               'for the human population to reach one <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Billion">billion</a> '
                               'and only 207 years more to grow to 7 '
                               'billion.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup> '
                               'The combined <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biomass_(ecology)">biomass</a> '
                               'of the carbon of all the humans on Earth in '
                               '2018 was estimated at 60 million tons, about '
                               '10 times larger than that of all '
                               'non-domesticated mammals.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bar-On-141">[139]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>In 2018, 4.2 billion humans (55%) lived in '
                               'urban areas, up from 751 million in '
                               '1950.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-United_Nations_Department_of_Economic_and_Social_Affairs_(DESA)-2018-150">[148]</a></sup> '
                               'The most urbanized regions are Northern '
                               'America (82%), Latin America (81%), Europe '
                               '(74%) and Oceania (68%), with Africa and Asia '
                               "having nearly 90% of the world's 3.4 billion "
                               'rural population.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-United_Nations_Department_of_Economic_and_Social_Affairs_(DESA)-2018-150">[148]</a></sup> '
                               'Problems for humans living in cities include '
                               'various forms of pollution and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crime">crime</a>,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup> '
                               'especially in inner city and suburban <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slum">slums</a>.</p>\n'
                               '<h2>Biology</h2>\n'
                               '<h3>Anatomy and physiology</h3>\n'
                               '<p>Main article: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_body">Human '
                               'body</a></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Anterior_view_of_human_female_and_male,_with_labels_2.png"><img '
                               'data-file-height="867" data-file-width="818" '
                               'src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Anterior_view_of_human_female_and_male%2C_with_labels_2.png/660px-Anterior_view_of_human_female_and_male%2C_with_labels_2.png" '
                               'srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Anterior_view_of_human_female_and_male%2C_with_labels_2.png/495px-Anterior_view_of_human_female_and_male%2C_with_labels_2.png '
                               '1.5x, '
                               '//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Anterior_view_of_human_female_and_male%2C_with_labels_2.png/660px-Anterior_view_of_human_female_and_male%2C_with_labels_2.png '
                               '2x"></img></a><figcaption>Basic anatomical '
                               'features of female and male humans. These '
                               'models have had <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Body_hair">body '
                               'hair</a> and male <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Facial_hair">facial '
                               'hair</a> removed and head hair '
                               'trimmed.</figcaption></figure>\n'
                               '<p>Most aspects of human physiology are '
                               'closely <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homology_(biology)">homologous</a> '
                               'to corresponding aspects of animal physiology. '
                               'The <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dental_formula">dental '
                               'formula</a> of humans is: 2.1.2.32.1.2.3. '
                               'Humans have proportionately shorter <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palate">palates</a> '
                               'and much smaller <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_tooth">teeth</a> '
                               'than other primates. They are the only '
                               'primates to have short, relatively flush <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canine_teeth">canine '
                               'teeth</a>. Humans have characteristically '
                               'crowded teeth, with gaps from lost teeth '
                               'usually closing up quickly in young '
                               'individuals. Humans are gradually losing their '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wisdom_teeth">third '
                               'molars</a>, with some individuals having them '
                               'congenitally absent.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Revolution-152">[150]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Humans share with chimpanzees a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vestigiality">vestigial</a> '
                               'tail,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup> '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Appendix_(anatomy)">appendix</a>, '
                               'flexible shoulder joints, grasping fingers and '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opposable_thumb">opposable '
                               'thumbs</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-154">[152]</a></sup> '
                               'Humans also have a more barrel-shaped chests '
                               'in contrast to the funnel shape of other apes, '
                               'an adaptation for bipedal respiration.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup> '
                               'Apart from bipedalism and brain size, humans '
                               'differ from chimpanzees mostly in <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smelling">smelling</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hearing">hearing</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digestion#Protein_digestion">digesting '
                               'proteins</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-O\'Neil-156">[154]</a></sup> '
                               'While humans have a density of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hair_follicle">hair '
                               'follicles</a> comparable to other apes, it is '
                               'predominantly <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vellus_hair">vellus '
                               'hair</a>, most of which is so short and wispy '
                               'as to be practically invisible.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-157">[155]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-158">[156]</a></sup> '
                               'Humans have about 2 million <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sweat_gland">sweat '
                               'glands</a> spread over their entire bodies, '
                               'many more than chimpanzees, whose sweat glands '
                               'are scarce and are mainly located on the palm '
                               'of the hand and on the soles of the '
                               'feet.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>It is estimated that the worldwide average '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_height">height '
                               'for an adult human</a> male is about 171 cm (5 '
                               'ft 7 in), while the worldwide average height '
                               'for adult human females is about 159 cm (5 ft '
                               '3 in).<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup> '
                               'Shrinkage of stature may begin in middle age '
                               'in some individuals but tends to be typical in '
                               'the extremely <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_age">aged</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-161">[159]</a></sup> '
                               'Throughout history, human populations have '
                               'universally become taller, probably as a '
                               'consequence of better nutrition, healthcare, '
                               'and living conditions.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-162">[160]</a></sup> '
                               'The average <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Body_weight">mass</a> '
                               'of an adult human is 59 kg (130 lb) for '
                               'females and 77 kg (170 lb) for males.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-163">[161]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-164">[162]</a></sup> '
                               'Like many other conditions, body weight and '
                               'body type are influenced by both <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_predisposition">genetic '
                               'susceptibility</a> and environment and varies '
                               'greatly among individuals.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-165">[163]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-166">[164]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Humans have a far faster and more accurate '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Throw">throw</a> '
                               'than other animals.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-167">[165]</a></sup> '
                               'Humans are also among the best long-distance '
                               'runners in the animal kingdom, but slower over '
                               'short distances.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-168">[166]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-O\'Neil-156">[154]</a></sup> '
                               "Humans' thinner body hair and more productive "
                               'sweat glands help avoid <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heat_exhaustion">heat '
                               'exhaustion</a> while running for long '
                               'distances.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-169">[167]</a></sup> '
                               'Compared to other apes, the human <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heart">heart</a> '
                               'produces greater <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stroke_volume">stroke '
                               'volume</a> and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cardiac_output">cardiac '
                               'output</a> and the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aorta">aorta</a> '
                               'is proportionately larger.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-170">[168]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-171">[169]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h3>Genetics</h3>\n'
                               '<p>Main article: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_genetics">Human '
                               'genetics</a></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Karyotype.png"><img '
                               'data-file-height="1159" data-file-width="1077" '
                               'src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Karyotype.png/440px-Karyotype.png" '
                               'srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Karyotype.png/330px-Karyotype.png '
                               '1.5x, '
                               '//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Karyotype.png/440px-Karyotype.png '
                               '2x"></img></a><figcaption>A graphical '
                               'representation of the standard human <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karyotype">karyotype</a>, '
                               'including both the female (XX) and male (XY) '
                               'sex chromosomes.</figcaption></figure>\n'
                               '<p>Like most animals, humans are a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ploidy">diploid</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eukaryote">eukaryotic</a> '
                               'species. Each <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Somatic_cell">somatic '
                               'cell</a> has two sets of 23 <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chromosome">chromosomes</a>, '
                               'each set received from one parent; <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gamete">gametes</a> '
                               'have only one set of chromosomes, which is a '
                               'mixture of the two parental sets. Among the 23 '
                               'pairs of chromosomes, there are 22 pairs of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autosome">autosomes</a> '
                               'and one pair of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sex-determination_system">sex '
                               'chromosomes</a>. Like other mammals, humans '
                               'have an <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/XY_sex-determination_system">XY '
                               'sex-determination system</a>, so that females '
                               'have the sex chromosomes XX and males have '
                               'XY.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-172">[170]</a></sup> '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gene">Genes</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environment_(biophysical)">environment</a> '
                               'influence human biological variation in '
                               'visible characteristics, physiology, disease '
                               'susceptibility and mental abilities. The exact '
                               'influence of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environment_(biophysical)">genes '
                               'and environment</a> on certain traits is not '
                               'well understood.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-173">[171]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>While no humans &ndash; not even <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monozygotic_twins">monozygotic '
                               'twins</a> &ndash; are genetically '
                               'identical,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-175">[173]</a></sup> '
                               'two humans on average will have a genetic '
                               'similarity of 99.5%-99.9%.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-176">[174]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-177">[175]</a></sup> '
                               'This makes them more <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_genetic_variation">homogeneous</a> '
                               'than other great apes, including '
                               'chimpanzees.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-REGWG2005-178">[176]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-179">[177]</a></sup> '
                               'This small variation in human DNA compared to '
                               'many other species suggests a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_bottleneck">population '
                               'bottleneck</a> during the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_Pleistocene">Late '
                               'Pleistocene</a> (around 100,000 years ago), in '
                               'which the human population was reduced to a '
                               'small number of breeding pairs.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-180">[178]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-181">[179]</a></sup> '
                               'The forces of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_selection">natural '
                               'selection</a> have continued to operate on '
                               'human populations, with evidence that certain '
                               'regions of the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genome">genome</a> '
                               'display <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Directional_selection">directional '
                               'selection</a> in the past 15,000 years.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>The <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_genome">human '
                               'genome</a> was first sequenced in 2001<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-183">[181]</a></sup> '
                               'and by 2020 hundreds of thousands of genomes '
                               'had been sequenced.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-184">[182]</a></sup> '
                               'In 2012 the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_HapMap_Project">International '
                               'HapMap Project</a> had compared the genomes of '
                               '1,184 individuals from 11 populations and '
                               'identified 1.6 million <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Single_nucleotide_polymorphisms">single '
                               'nucleotide polymorphisms</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup> '
                               'African populations harbor the highest number '
                               'of private genetic variants. While many of the '
                               'common variants found in populations outside '
                               'of Africa are also found on the African '
                               'continent, there are still large numbers that '
                               'are private to these regions, especially <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oceania">Oceania</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Americas">the '
                               'Americas</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bergstrom2020-186">[184]</a></sup> '
                               'By 2010 estimates, humans have approximately '
                               '22,000 genes.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-187">[185]</a></sup> '
                               'By comparing <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MtDNA">mitochondrial '
                               'DNA</a>, which is inherited only from the '
                               'mother, geneticists have concluded that the '
                               'last female common ancestor whose <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_marker">genetic '
                               'marker</a> is found in all modern humans, the '
                               'so-called <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mitochondrial_Eve">mitochondrial '
                               'Eve</a>, must have lived around 90,000 to '
                               '200,000 years ago.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-188">[186]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-189">[187]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-190">[188]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-191">[189]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h3>Life cycle</h3>\n'
                               '<p>See also: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Childbirth">Childbirth</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life_expectancy">Life '
                               'expectancy</a></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Tubal_Pregnancy_with_embryo.jpg"><img '
                               'data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="1874" '
                               'src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Tubal_Pregnancy_with_embryo.jpg/440px-Tubal_Pregnancy_with_embryo.jpg" '
                               'srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Tubal_Pregnancy_with_embryo.jpg/330px-Tubal_Pregnancy_with_embryo.jpg '
                               '1.5x, '
                               '//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Tubal_Pregnancy_with_embryo.jpg/440px-Tubal_Pregnancy_with_embryo.jpg '
                               '2x"></img></a><figcaption>A 10 mm <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_embryo">human '
                               'embryo</a> at 5 weeks</figcaption></figure>\n'
                               '<p>Most <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_reproduction">human '
                               'reproduction</a> takes place by <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internal_fertilization">internal '
                               'fertilization</a> via <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_sexual_intercourse">sexual '
                               'intercourse</a>, but can also occur through <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assisted_reproductive_technology">assisted '
                               'reproductive technology</a> procedures.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-192">[190]</a></sup> '
                               'The average <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gestation">gestation</a> '
                               'period is 38 weeks, but a normal pregnancy can '
                               'vary by up to 37 days.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-193">[191]</a></sup> '
                               'Embryonic development in the human covers the '
                               'first eight weeks of development; at the '
                               'beginning of the ninth week the embryo is '
                               'termed a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fetus">fetus</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-194">[192]</a></sup> '
                               'Humans are able to <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labor_induction">induce '
                               'early labor</a> or perform a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caesarean_section">caesarean '
                               'section</a> if the child needs to be born '
                               'earlier for medical reasons.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-195">[193]</a></sup> '
                               'In developed countries, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infant">infants</a> '
                               'are typically 3&ndash;4 kg (7&ndash;9 lb) in '
                               'weight and 47&ndash;53 cm (19&ndash;21 in) in '
                               'height at birth.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-196">[194]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-197">[195]</a></sup> '
                               'However, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Low_birth_weight">low '
                               'birth weight</a> is common in developing '
                               'countries, and contributes to the high levels '
                               'of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infant_mortality">infant '
                               'mortality</a> in these regions.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-198">[196]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Compared with other species, human '
                               'childbirth is dangerous, with a much higher '
                               'risk of complications and death.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-199">[197]</a></sup> '
                               "The size of the fetus's head is more closely "
                               'matched to the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pelvis">pelvis</a> '
                               'than in other primates.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Pavlicev-200">[198]</a></sup> '
                               'The reason for this is not completely '
                               'understood,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-202">[n '
                               '3]</a></sup> but it contributes to a painful '
                               'labor that can last 24 hours or more.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-203">[200]</a></sup> '
                               'The chances of a successful labor increased '
                               'significantly during the 20th century in '
                               'wealthier countries with the advent of new '
                               'medical technologies. In contrast, pregnancy '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_childbirth">natural '
                               'childbirth</a> remain hazardous ordeals in '
                               'developing regions of the world, with <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maternal_death_rates">maternal '
                               'death rates</a> approximately 100 times '
                               'greater than in developed countries.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-204">[201]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Both the mother and the father provide care '
                               'for human offspring, in contrast to other '
                               'primates, where parental care is mostly done '
                               'by the mother.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-205">[202]</a></sup> '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Altricial">Helpless '
                               'at birth</a>, humans continue to grow for some '
                               'years, typically reaching <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_maturity">sexual '
                               'maturity</a> at 15 to 17 years of age.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-206">[203]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-207">[204]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-208">[205]</a></sup> '
                               'The human life span has been split into '
                               'various stages ranging from three to twelve. '
                               'Common stages include <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infant">infancy</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Childhood">childhood</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolescence">adolescence</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adult">adulthood</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_age">old '
                               'age</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-209">[206]</a></sup> '
                               'The lengths of these stages have varied across '
                               'cultures and time periods but is typified by '
                               'an unusually rapid growth spurt during '
                               'adolescence.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-210">[207]</a></sup> '
                               'Human females undergo <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Menopause">menopause</a> '
                               'and become <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infertility">infertile</a> '
                               'at around the age of 50.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-211">[208]</a></sup> '
                               'It has been proposed that menopause increases '
                               "a woman's overall reproductive success by "
                               'allowing her to invest more time and resources '
                               'in her existing offspring, and in turn their '
                               'children (the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grandmother_hypothesis">grandmother '
                               'hypothesis</a>), rather than by continuing to '
                               'bear children into old age.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-212">[209]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-213">[210]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>The life span of an individual depends on '
                               'two major factors, genetics and lifestyle '
                               'choices.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-214">[211]</a></sup> '
                               'For various reasons, including '
                               'biological/genetic causes, women live on '
                               'average about four years longer than '
                               'men.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-215">[212]</a></sup> '
                               'As of 2018, the global average <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life_expectancy_at_birth">life '
                               'expectancy at birth</a> of a girl is estimated '
                               'to be 74.9 years compared to 70.4 for a '
                               'boy.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-216">[213]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-217">[214]</a></sup> '
                               'There are significant geographical variations '
                               'in human life expectancy, mostly correlated '
                               'with economic development &ndash; for example, '
                               'life expectancy at birth in <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hong_Kong">Hong '
                               'Kong</a> is 87.6 years for girls and 81.8 for '
                               'boys, while in the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_African_Republic">Central '
                               'African Republic</a>, it is 55.0 years for '
                               'girls and 50.6 for boys.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-218">[215]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-219">[216]</a></sup> '
                               'The developed world is generally aging, with '
                               'the median age around 40 years. In the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_world">developing '
                               'world</a>, the median age is between 15 and 20 '
                               'years. While one in five Europeans is 60 years '
                               'of age or older, only one in twenty Africans '
                               'is 60 years of age or older.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-220">[217]</a></sup> '
                               'In 2012, the United Nations estimated that '
                               'there were 316,600 living <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centenarians">centenarians</a> '
                               '(humans of age 100 or older) worldwide.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-221">[218]</a></sup></p>\n'
