                               '<h3>Diet</h3>\n'
                               '<p>Main article: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_nutrition">Human '
                               'nutrition</a></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Preparing_The_Feast.jpg"><img '
                               'data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" '
                               'src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Preparing_The_Feast.jpg/440px-Preparing_The_Feast.jpg" '
                               'srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Preparing_The_Feast.jpg/330px-Preparing_The_Feast.jpg '
                               '1.5x, '
                               '//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Preparing_The_Feast.jpg/440px-Preparing_The_Feast.jpg '
                               '2x"></img></a><figcaption>Humans living in <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bali">Bali</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, '
                               'preparing a meal</figcaption></figure>\n'
                               '<p>Humans are <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Omnivorous">omnivorous</a>,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-222">[219]</a></sup> '
                               'capable of consuming a wide variety of plant '
                               'and animal material.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-223">[220]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-224">[221]</a></sup> '
                               'Human groups have adopted a range of diets '
                               'from purely <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vegan">vegan</a> '
                               'to primarily <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carnivorous">carnivorous</a>. '
                               'In some cases, dietary restrictions in humans '
                               'can lead to <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deficiency_diseases">deficiency '
                               'diseases</a>; however, stable human groups '
                               'have adapted to many dietary patterns through '
                               'both genetic specialization and cultural '
                               'conventions to use nutritionally balanced food '
                               'sources.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-225">[222]</a></sup> '
                               'The human diet is prominently reflected in '
                               'human culture and has led to the development '
                               'of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Food_science">food '
                               'science</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Crittenden-2017-226">[223]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Until the development of agriculture, '
                               '<i>Homo sapiens</i> employed a hunter-gatherer '
                               'method as their sole means of food '
                               'collection.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Crittenden-2017-226">[223]</a></sup> '
                               'This involved combining stationary food '
                               'sources (such as fruits, grains, tubers, and '
                               'mushrooms, insect larvae and aquatic mollusks) '
                               'with <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Game_(food)">wild '
                               'game</a>, which must be hunted and captured in '
                               'order to be consumed.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-227">[224]</a></sup> '
                               'It has been proposed that humans have used '
                               'fire to prepare and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cooking">cook</a> '
                               'food since the time of <i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo_erectus">Homo '
                               'erectus</a></i>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-228">[225]</a></sup> '
                               'Human <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domestication">domestication</a> '
                               'of wild plants began about 11,700 years ago, '
                               'leading to the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_agriculture">development '
                               'of agriculture</a>,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-229">[226]</a></sup> '
                               'a gradual process called the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution">Neolithic '
                               'Revolution</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-230">[227]</a></sup> '
                               'These dietary changes may also have altered '
                               'human biology; the spread of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dairy_farming">dairy '
                               'farming</a> provided a new and rich source of '
                               'food, leading to the evolution of the ability '
                               'to digest <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lactose">lactose</a> '
                               'in some adults.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-231">[228]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-232">[229]</a></sup> '
                               'The types of food consumed, and how they are '
                               'prepared, have varied widely by time, '
                               'location, and culture.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-233">[230]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-234">[231]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>In general, humans can survive for up to '
                               'eight weeks without food, depending on stored '
                               'body fat.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-235">[232]</a></sup> '
                               'Survival without water is usually limited to '
                               'three or four days, with a maximum of one '
                               'week.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-236">[233]</a></sup> '
                               'In 2020 it is estimated 9 million humans die '
                               'every year from causes directly or indirectly '
                               'related to <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Starvation">starvation</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-237">[234]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-238">[235]</a></sup> '
                               'Childhood malnutrition is also common and '
                               'contributes to the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disease_burden">global '
                               'burden of disease</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-239">[236]</a></sup> '
                               'However, global food distribution is not even, '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Obesity">obesity</a> '
                               'among some human populations has increased '
                               'rapidly, leading to health complications and '
                               'increased mortality in some <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Developed_country">developed</a> '
                               'and a few <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Developing_countries">developing '
                               'countries</a>. Worldwide, over one billion '
                               'people are obese,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Haslam-240">[237]</a></sup> '
                               'while in the United States 35% of people are '
                               'obese, leading to this being described as an '
                               '&quot;<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epidemiology_of_obesity">obesity '
                               'epidemic</a>.&quot;<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-241">[238]</a></sup> '
                               'Obesity is caused by consuming more <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calorie">calories</a> '
                               'than are expended, so excessive weight gain is '
                               'usually caused by an energy-dense diet.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Haslam-240">[237]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h3>Biological variation</h3>\n'
                               '<p>Main article: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_genetic_variation">Human '
                               'genetic variation</a></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Seti1a.jpg"><img '
                               'data-file-height="253" data-file-width="377" '
                               'src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/ce/Seti1a.jpg" '
                               'srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Seti1a.jpg/330px-Seti1a.jpg '
                               '1.5x, '
                               '//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/ce/Seti1a.jpg '
                               '2x"></img></a><figcaption>A <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berbers">Libyan</a>, '
                               'a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nubians">Nubian</a>, '
                               'a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syrian_people">Syrian</a>, '
                               'and an <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egyptians">Egyptian</a>, '
                               'drawing by an unknown artist after a mural of '
                               'the tomb of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seti_I">Seti '
                               'I</a></figcaption></figure>\n'
                               '<p>There is biological variation in the human '
                               'species &ndash; with traits such as <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood_type">blood '
                               'type</a>, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_diseases">genetic '
                               'diseases</a>, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_skull">cranial '
                               'features</a>, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_face">facial '
                               'features</a>, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organ_systems">organ '
                               'systems</a>, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eye_color">eye '
                               'color</a>, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hair_color">hair '
                               'color</a> and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hair_texture">texture</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_height">height</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Body_shape">build</a>, '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_skin_color">skin '
                               'color</a> varying across the globe. The '
                               'typical height of an adult human is between '
                               '1.4 and 1.9 m (4 ft 7 in and 6 ft 3 in), '
                               'although this varies significantly depending '
                               'on sex, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_origin">ethnic '
                               'origin</a>, and family bloodlines.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-242">[239]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-243">[240]</a></sup> '
                               'Body size is partly determined by genes and is '
                               'also significantly influenced by environmental '
                               'factors such as <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diet_(nutrition)">diet</a>, '
                               'exercise, and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sleep_pattern">sleep '
                               'patterns</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-244">[241]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Hair_colors.jpg"><img '
                               'data-file-height="5081" data-file-width="3446" '
                               'src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Hair_colors.jpg/440px-Hair_colors.jpg" '
                               'srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Hair_colors.jpg/330px-Hair_colors.jpg '
                               '1.5x, '
                               '//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Hair_colors.jpg/440px-Hair_colors.jpg '
                               '2x"></img></a><figcaption>A variety of human '
                               'hair colors; from top left, clockwise: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_hair">black</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brown_hair">brown</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blond">blonde</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_hair">white</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_hair">red</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n'
                               '<p>There is evidence that populations have '
                               'adapted genetically to various external '
                               'factors. The genes that allow adult humans to '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lactose_tolerance">digest '
                               'lactose</a> are present in high frequencies in '
                               'populations that have long histories of cattle '
                               'domestication and are more dependent on <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cow_milk">cow '
                               'milk</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-245">[242]</a></sup> '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sickle_cell_anemia">Sickle '
                               'cell anemia</a>, which may provide increased '
                               'resistance to <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malaria">malaria</a>, '
                               'is frequent in populations where <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malaria">malaria</a> '
                               'is endemic.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-246">[243]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-247">[244]</a></sup> '
                               'Populations that have for a very long time '
                               'inhabited specific climates tend to have '
                               'developed specific <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phenotype">phenotypes</a> '
                               'that are beneficial for those environments '
                               '&ndash; <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allen%27s_rule">short '
                               'stature and stocky build in cold regions</a>, '
                               'tall and lanky in hot regions, and with high '
                               'lung capacities or other <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High-altitude_adaptation_in_humans">adaptations '
                               'at high altitudes</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-248">[245]</a></sup> '
                               'Some populations have evolved highly unique '
                               'adaptations to very specific environmental '
                               'conditions, such as those advantageous to '
                               'ocean-dwelling lifestyles and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freediving">freediving</a> '
                               'in the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bajau">Bajau</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-249">[246]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Human hair ranges in color from <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_hair">red</a> '
                               'to <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blond">blond</a> '
                               'to <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brown_hair">brown</a> '
                               'to <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_hair">black</a>, '
                               'which is the most frequent.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-250">[247]</a></sup> '
                               'Hair color depends on the amount of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Melanin">melanin</a>, '
                               'with concentrations fading with increased age, '
                               'leading to <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grey_hair">grey</a> '
                               'or even white hair. Skin color can range from '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dark_skin">darkest '
                               'brown</a> to <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light_skin">lightest '
                               'peach</a>, or even nearly white or colorless '
                               'in cases of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albinism">albinism</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-roberts1-251">[248]</a></sup> '
                               'It tends to vary <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clinal_variation">clinally</a> '
                               'and generally correlates with the level of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultraviolet">ultraviolet '
                               'radiation</a> in a particular geographic area, '
                               'with darker skin mostly around the '
                               'equator.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-252">[249]</a></sup> '
                               'Skin darkening may have evolved as protection '
                               'against ultraviolet solar radiation.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-253">[250]</a></sup> '
                               'Light skin pigmentation protects against '
                               'depletion of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vitamin_D">vitamin '
                               'D</a>, which requires <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sunlight">sunlight</a> '
                               'to make.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-254">[251]</a></sup> '
                               'Human skin also has a capacity to darken (tan) '
                               'in response to exposure to ultraviolet '
                               'radiation.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-255">[252]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-256">[253]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>There is relatively little variation '
                               'between human geographical populations, and '
                               'most of the variation that occurs is at the '
                               'individual level.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-roberts1-251">[248]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-257">[254]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-258">[255]</a></sup> '
                               'Much of human variation is continuous, often '
                               'with no clear points of demarcation.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-259">[256]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-260">[257]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-261">[258]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-262">[259]</a></sup> '
                               'Genetic data shows that no matter how '
                               'population groups are defined, two people from '
                               'the same population group are almost as '
                               'different from each other as two people from '
                               'any two different population groups.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-263">[260]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-264">[261]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-265">[262]</a></sup> '
                               'Dark-skinned populations that are found in '
                               'Africa, Australia, and South Asia are not '
                               'closely related to each other.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-266">[263]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-267">[264]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Genetic research has demonstrated that '
                               'human populations native to the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African_continent">African '
                               'continent</a> are the most genetically '
                               'diverse<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-268">[265]</a></sup> '
                               'and genetic diversity decreases with migratory '
                               'distance from Africa, possibly the result of '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_bottleneck">bottlenecks</a> '
                               'during human migration.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-269">[266]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-270">[267]</a></sup> '
                               'These non-African populations acquired new '
                               'genetic inputs from local <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interbreeding_between_archaic_and_modern_humans">admixture '
                               'with archaic populations</a> and have much '
                               'greater variation from <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neanderthals">Neanderthals</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denisovans">Denisovans</a> '
                               'than is found in Africa,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bergstrom2020-186">[184]</a></sup> '
                               'though Neanderthal admixture into African '
                               'populations may be underestimated.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-271">[268]</a></sup> '
                               'Furthermore, recent studies have found that '
                               'populations in <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa">sub-Saharan '
                               'Africa</a>, and particularly <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Africa">West '
                               'Africa</a>, have ancestral genetic variation '
                               'which predates modern humans and has been lost '
                               'in most non-African populations. Some of this '
                               'ancestry is thought to originate from '
                               'admixture with an <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interbreeding_between_archaic_and_modern_humans#Archaic_African_hominins">unknown '
                               'archaic hominin</a> that diverged before the '
                               'split of Neanderthals and modern '
                               'humans.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-272">[269]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-273">[270]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Humans are a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gonochorism">gonochoric</a> '
                               'species, meaning they are divided into male '
                               'and female <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sex">sexes</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-274">[271]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-275">[272]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-276">[273]</a></sup> '
                               'The greatest degree of genetic <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sex_differences_in_humans">variation '
                               'exists between males and females</a>. While '
                               'the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleotide_diversity">nucleotide</a> '
                               'genetic variation of individuals of the same '
                               'sex across global populations is no greater '
                               'than 0.1%&ndash;0.5%, the genetic difference '
                               'between <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Man">males</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Woman">females</a> '
                               'is between 1% and 2%. Males on average are 15% '
                               'heavier and 15 cm (6 in) taller than '
                               'females.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-277">[274]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-278">[275]</a></sup> '
                               'On average, men have about 40&ndash;50% more '
                               'upper-body strength and 20&ndash;30% more '
                               'lower-body strength than women at the same '
                               'weight, due to higher amounts of muscle and '
                               'larger muscle fibers.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-279">[276]</a></sup> '
                               'Women generally have a higher <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Body_fat">body '
                               'fat</a> percentage than men.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-280">[277]</a></sup> '
                               'Women have <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_skin_color#Sexual_dimorphism">lighter '
                               'skin</a> than men of the same population; this '
                               'has been explained by a higher need for '
                               'vitamin D in females during pregnancy and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lactation">lactation</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-281">[278]</a></sup> '
                               'As there are chromosomal differences between '
                               'females and males, some X and Y '
                               'chromosome-related conditions and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disease">disorders</a> '
                               'only affect either men or women.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-282">[279]</a></sup> '
                               'After allowing for body weight and volume, the '
                               'male voice is usually an <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Octave">octave</a> '
                               'deeper than the female voice.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-283">[280]</a></sup> '
                               'Women have a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sex_differences_in_longevity">longer '
                               'life span</a> in almost every population '
                               'around the world.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-284">[281]</a></sup> '
                               'There are <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intersex">intersex</a> '
                               'conditions in the human population, however '
                               'these are rare.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-285">[282]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-286">[283]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h2>Psychology</h2>\n'
                               '<p>Main article: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psychology">Psychology</a></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:NIA_human_brain_drawing.jpg"><img '
                               'data-file-height="637" data-file-width="559" '
                               'src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/NIA_human_brain_drawing.jpg/440px-NIA_human_brain_drawing.jpg" '
                               'srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/NIA_human_brain_drawing.jpg/330px-NIA_human_brain_drawing.jpg '
                               '1.5x, '
                               '//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/NIA_human_brain_drawing.jpg/440px-NIA_human_brain_drawing.jpg '
                               '2x"></img></a><figcaption>Drawing of the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_brain">human '
                               'brain</a>, showing several important '
                               'structures</figcaption></figure>\n'
                               '<p>The <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_brain">human '
                               'brain</a>, the focal point of the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_nervous_system">central '
                               'nervous system</a> in humans, controls the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peripheral_nervous_system">peripheral '
                               'nervous system</a>. In addition to controlling '
                               '&quot;lower&quot;, involuntary, or primarily '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autonomic_nervous_system">autonomic</a> '
                               'activities such as <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Respiration_(physiology)">respiration</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digestion">digestion</a>, '
                               'it is also the locus of &quot;higher&quot; '
                               'order functioning such as <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thought">thought</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reason">reasoning</a>, '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abstraction">abstraction</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-287">[284]</a></sup> '
                               'These <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mental_function">cognitive '
                               'processes</a> constitute the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mind">mind</a>, '
                               'and, along with their <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Behavior">behavioral</a> '
                               'consequences, are studied in the field of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psychology">psychology</a>.</p>\n'
                               '<p>Humans have a larger and more developed <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prefrontal_cortex">prefrontal '
                               'cortex</a> than other primates, the region of '
                               'the brain associated with higher <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognition">cognition</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-288">[285]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-289">[286]</a></sup> '
                               'This has led humans to proclaim themselves to '
                               'be more intelligent than any other known '
                               'species.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-290">[287]</a></sup> '
                               'Objectively defining intelligence is '
                               'difficult, with other animals adapting senses '
                               'and excelling in areas that humans are unable '
                               'to.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-291">[288]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>There are some traits that, although not '
                               'strictly unique, do set humans apart from '
                               'other animals.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-292">[289]</a></sup> '
                               'Humans may be the only animals who have <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Episodic_memory#In_animals">episodic '
                               'memory</a> and who can engage in &quot;<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mental_time_travel#Evolution_and_human_uniqueness">mental '
                               'time travel</a>&quot;.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-293">[290]</a></sup> '
                               'Even compared with other social animals, '
                               'humans have an unusually high degree of '
                               'flexibility in their facial '
                               'expressions.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-294">[291]</a></sup> '
                               'Humans are the only animals known to cry '
                               'emotional tears.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-295">[292]</a></sup> '
                               'Humans are one of the few animals able to '
                               'self-recognize in <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mirror_test">mirror '
                               'tests</a><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-296">[293]</a></sup> '
                               'and there is also debate over to what extent '
                               'humans are the only animals with a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theory_of_mind">theory '
                               'of mind</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-297">[294]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-298">[295]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h3>Sleep and dreaming</h3>\n'
                               '<p>Main articles: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sleep">Sleep</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dream">Dream</a></p>\n'
                               '<p>Humans are generally <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diurnality">diurnal</a>. '
                               'The average sleep requirement is between seven '
                               'and nine hours per day for an adult and nine '
                               'to ten hours per day for a child; elderly '
                               'people usually sleep for six to seven hours. '
                               'Having less sleep than this is common among '
                               'humans, even though <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sleep_deprivation">sleep '
                               'deprivation</a> can have negative health '
                               'effects. A sustained restriction of adult '
                               'sleep to four hours per day has been shown to '
                               'correlate with changes in physiology and '
                               'mental state, including reduced memory, '
                               'fatigue, aggression, and bodily '
                               'discomfort.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-299">[296]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>During sleep humans dream, where they '
                               'experience sensory images and sounds. Dreaming '
                               'is stimulated by the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pons">pons</a> '
                               'and mostly occurs during the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/REM_phase_of_sleep">REM '
                               'phase of sleep</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-300">[297]</a></sup> '
                               'The length of a dream can vary, from a few '
                               'seconds up to 30 minutes.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-301">[298]</a></sup> '
                               'Humans have three to five dreams per night, '
                               'and some may have up to seven.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-302">[299]</a></sup> '
                               'Dreamers are more likely to remember the dream '
                               'if awakened during the REM phase. The events '
                               'in dreams are generally outside the control of '
                               'the dreamer, with the exception of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucid_dream">lucid '
                               'dreaming</a>, where the dreamer is <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-aware">self-aware</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-303">[300]</a></sup> '
                               'Dreams can at times make a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Creativity">creative</a> '
                               'thought occur or give a sense of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artistic_inspiration">inspiration</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-304">[301]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h3>Consciousness and thought</h3>\n'
                               '<p>Main articles: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consciousness">Consciousness</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognition">Cognition</a></p>\n'
                               '<p>Human consciousness, at its simplest, is <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sentience">sentience</a> '
                               'or <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Awareness">awareness</a> '
                               'of internal or external existence.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-305">[302]</a></sup> '
                               'Despite centuries of analyses, definitions, '
                               'explanations and debates by philosophers and '
                               'scientists, consciousness remains puzzling and '
                               'controversial,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-306">[303]</a></sup> '
                               'being &quot;at once the most familiar and most '
                               'mysterious aspect of our lives&quot;.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-307">[304]</a></sup> '
                               'The only widely agreed notion about the topic '
                               'is the intuition that it exists.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-308">[305]</a></sup> '
                               'Opinions differ about what exactly needs to be '
                               'studied and explained as consciousness. Some '
                               'philosophers divide consciousness into '
                               'phenomenal consciousness, which is sensory '
                               'experience itself, and access consciousness, '
                               'which can be used for reasoning or directly '
                               'controlling actions.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-309">[306]</a></sup> '
                               "It is sometimes synonymous with 'the mind', "
                               'and at other times, an aspect of it. '
                               'Historically it is associated with <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Introspection">introspection</a>, '
                               'private <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thought">thought</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imagination">imagination</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volition_(psychology)">volition</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-310">[307]</a></sup> '
                               'It now often includes some kind of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Experience">experience</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognition">cognition</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feeling">feeling</a> '
                               'or <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perception">perception</a>. '
                               "It may be 'awareness', or '<a "
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meta-cognition">awareness '
                               "of awareness</a>', or <a "
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-awareness">self-awareness</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-311">[308]</a></sup> '
                               'There might be different levels or <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Higher-order_theories_of_consciousness">orders '
                               'of consciousness</a>,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-312">[309]</a></sup> '
                               'or different kinds of consciousness, or just '
                               'one kind with different features.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-313">[310]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>The process of acquiring knowledge and '
                               'understanding through thought, experience, and '
                               'the senses is known as cognition.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-314">[311]</a></sup> '
                               'The human brain <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perception">perceives</a> '
                               'the external world through the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sense">senses</a>, '
                               'and each individual human is influenced '
                               'greatly by his or her experiences, leading to '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subjectivity">subjective</a> '
                               'views of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Existence">existence</a> '
                               'and the passage of time.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-315">[312]</a></sup> '
                               'The nature of thought is central to psychology '
                               'and related fields. <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_psychology">Cognitive '
                               'psychology</a> studies <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognition">cognition</a>, '
                               'the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mental_function">mental '
                               'processes</a> underlying behavior.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-316">[313]</a></sup> '
                               'Largely focusing on the development of the '
                               'human mind through the life span, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Developmental_psychology">developmental '
                               'psychology</a> seeks to understand how people '
                               'come to perceive, understand, and act within '
                               'the world and how these processes change as '
                               'they age.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-317">[314]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-318">[315]</a></sup> '
                               'This may focus on intellectual, cognitive, '
                               'neural, social, or <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moral_development">moral '
                               'development</a>. <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psychologists">Psychologists</a> '
                               'have developed intelligence tests and the '
                               'concept of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligence_quotient">intelligence '
                               'quotient</a> in order to assess the relative '
                               'intelligence of human beings and study its <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distribution_(mathematics)">distribution</a> '
                               'among population.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-319">[316]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h3>Motivation and emotion</h3>\n'
                               '<p>Main articles: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Motivation">Motivation</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emotion">Emotion</a></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Plate_depicting_emotions_of_grief_from_Charles_Darwin%27s_book_The_Expression_of_the_Emotions.jpg"><img '
                               'data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1142" '
                               'src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Plate_depicting_emotions_of_grief_from_Charles_Darwin%27s_book_The_Expression_of_the_Emotions.jpg/440px-Plate_depicting_emotions_of_grief_from_Charles_Darwin%27s_book_The_Expression_of_the_Emotions.jpg" '
                               'srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Plate_depicting_emotions_of_grief_from_Charles_Darwin%27s_book_The_Expression_of_the_Emotions.jpg/330px-Plate_depicting_emotions_of_grief_from_Charles_Darwin%27s_book_The_Expression_of_the_Emotions.jpg '
                               '1.5x, '
                               '//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Plate_depicting_emotions_of_grief_from_Charles_Darwin%27s_book_The_Expression_of_the_Emotions.jpg/440px-Plate_depicting_emotions_of_grief_from_Charles_Darwin%27s_book_The_Expression_of_the_Emotions.jpg '
                               '2x"></img></a><figcaption>Illustration of '
                               'grief from <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_Darwin">Charles '
                               "Darwin</a>'s 1872 book <i><a "
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Expression_of_the_Emotions_in_Man_and_Animals">The '
                               'Expression of the Emotions in Man and '
                               'Animals</a></i></figcaption></figure>\n'
                               '<p>Human motivation is not yet wholly '
                               'understood. From a psychological perspective, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maslow%27s_hierarchy_of_needs">Maslow\'s '
                               'hierarchy of needs</a> is a well-established '
                               'theory that can be defined as the process of '
                               'satisfying certain needs in ascending order of '
                               'complexity.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-320">[317]</a></sup> '
                               'From a more general, philosophical '
                               'perspective, human motivation can be defined '
                               'as a commitment to, or withdrawal from, '
                               'various goals requiring the application of '
                               'human ability. Furthermore, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Incentive">incentive</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Preference">preference</a> '
                               'are both factors, as are any perceived links '
                               'between incentives and preferences. <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volition_(psychology)">Volition</a> '
                               'may also be involved, in which case willpower '
                               'is also a factor. Ideally, both motivation and '
                               'volition ensure the selection, striving for, '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Realisation_(metrology)">realization</a> '
                               'of goals in an optimal manner, a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Function_(biology)">function</a> '
                               'beginning in childhood and continuing '
                               'throughout a lifetime in a process known as <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialization">socialization</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-321">[318]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Emotions are <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological">biological</a> '
                               'states associated with the nervous '
                               'system<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-322">[319]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-323">[320]</a></sup> '
                               'brought on by <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neurophysiology">neurophysiological</a> '
                               'changes variously associated with thoughts, '
                               'feelings, behavioral responses, and a degree '
                               'of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pleasure">pleasure</a> '
                               'or <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suffering">displeasure</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-324">[321]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-325">[322]</a></sup> '
                               'They are often <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reciprocal_influence">intertwined</a> '
                               'with <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mood_(psychology)">mood</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temperament">temperament</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Personality_psychology">personality</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disposition">disposition</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Creativity">creativity</a>,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-326">[323]</a></sup> '
                               'and motivation. Emotion has a significant '
                               'influence on human behavior and their ability '
                               'to learn.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-327">[324]</a></sup> '
                               'Acting on extreme or uncontrolled emotions can '
                               'lead to social disorder and crime,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-328">[325]</a></sup> '
                               'with studies showing criminals may have a '
                               'lower <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emotional_intelligence">emotional '
                               'intelligence</a> than normal.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-329">[326]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Emotional experiences perceived as <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pleasure">pleasant</a>, '
                               'such as <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joy">joy</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interest_(emotion)">interest</a> '
                               'or <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contentment">contentment</a>, '
                               'contrast with those perceived as <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suffering">unpleasant</a>, '
                               'like <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anxiety">anxiety</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sadness">sadness</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anger">anger</a>, '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)">despair</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-330">[327]</a></sup> '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Happiness">Happiness</a>, '
                               'or the state of being happy, is a human '
                               'emotional condition. The definition of '
                               'happiness is a common philosophical topic. '
                               'Some define it as experiencing the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feeling">feeling</a> '
                               'of positive <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Affect_(psychology)">emotional '
                               'affects</a>, while avoiding the negative '
                               'ones.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-331">[328]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-332">[329]</a></sup> '
                               'Others see it as an appraisal of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life_satisfaction">life '
                               'satisfaction</a> or <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quality_of_life">quality '
                               'of life</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-333">[330]</a></sup> '
                               'Recent research suggests that being happy '
                               'might involve experiencing some negative '
                               'emotions when humans feel they are '
                               'warranted.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-334">[331]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h3>Sexuality and love</h3>\n'
                               '<p>Main articles: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_sexuality">Human '
                               'sexuality</a> and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Love">Love</a></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sweet_Baby_Kisses_Family_Love.jpg"><img '
                               'data-file-height="2782" data-file-width="4133" '
                               'src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Sweet_Baby_Kisses_Family_Love.jpg/440px-Sweet_Baby_Kisses_Family_Love.jpg" '
                               'srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Sweet_Baby_Kisses_Family_Love.jpg/330px-Sweet_Baby_Kisses_Family_Love.jpg '
                               '1.5x, '
                               '//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Sweet_Baby_Kisses_Family_Love.jpg/440px-Sweet_Baby_Kisses_Family_Love.jpg '
                               '2x"></img></a><figcaption>Human parents often '
                               'display <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Familial_love">familial '
                               'love</a> for their '
                               'children.</figcaption></figure>\n'
                               '<p>For humans, sexuality involves <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological">biological</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erotic">erotic</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physical_intimacy">physical</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emotional_intimacy">emotional</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social">social</a>, '
                               'or <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spirituality">spiritual</a> '
                               'feelings and behaviors.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-S._Greenberg-335">[332]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bolin-336">[333]</a></sup> '
                               'Because it is a broad term, which has varied '
                               'with historical contexts over time, it lacks a '
                               'precise definition.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bolin-336">[333]</a></sup> '
                               'The biological and physical aspects of '
                               'sexuality largely concern the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_reproduction">human '
                               'reproductive functions</a>, including the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_sexual_response_cycle">human '
                               'sexual response cycle</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-S._Greenberg-335">[332]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bolin-336">[333]</a></sup> '
                               'Sexuality also affects and is affected by '
                               'cultural, political, legal, philosophical, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morality">moral</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethical">ethical</a>, '
                               'and religious aspects of life.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-S._Greenberg-335">[332]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bolin-336">[333]</a></sup> '
                               'Sexual desire, or <i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libido">libido</a></i>, '
                               'is a basic mental state present at the '
                               'beginning of sexual behavior. Studies show '
                               'that men desire sex more than women and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masturbation">masturbate</a> '
                               'more often.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-337">[334]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Humans can fall anywhere along a continuous '
                               'scale of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_orientation">sexual '
                               'orientation</a>,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-338">[335]</a></sup> '
                               'although most humans are <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heterosexual">heterosexual</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bailey16-339">[336]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-LeVay-340">[337]</a></sup> '
                               'While <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homosexuality">homosexual</a> '
                               'behavior <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homosexual_behavior_in_animals">occurs '
                               'in some other animals</a>, only humans and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheep">domestic '
                               'sheep</a> have so far been found to exhibit '
                               'exclusive preference for same-sex '
                               'relationships.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bailey16-339">[336]</a></sup> '
                               'Most evidence supports nonsocial, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biology_and_sexual_orientation">biological '
                               'causes of sexual orientation</a>,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bailey16-339">[336]</a></sup> '
                               'as cultures that are very tolerant of '
                               'homosexuality do not have significantly higher '
                               'rates of it.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-LeVay-340">[337]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-341">[338]</a></sup> '
                               'Research in <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuroscience">neuroscience</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetics">genetics</a> '
                               'suggests that other aspects of human sexuality '
                               'are biologically influenced as well.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-342">[339]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Love most commonly refers to a feeling of '
                               'strong attraction or emotional <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attachment_(psychology)">attachment</a>. '
                               'It can be impersonal (the love of an object, '
                               'ideal, or strong political or spiritual '
                               'connection) or interpersonal (love between '
                               'humans).<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-343">[340]</a></sup> '
                               'When in love <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dopamine">dopamine</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norepinephrine">norepinephrine</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serotonin">serotonin</a> '
                               "and other chemicals stimulate the brain's <a "
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pleasure_center">pleasure '
                               'center</a>, leading to side effects such as '
                               'increased <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heart_rate">heart '
                               'rate</a>, loss of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anorexia_(symptom)">appetite</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Insomnia">sleep</a>, '
                               'and an <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euphoria">intense '
                               'feeling of excitement</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-344">[341]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h2>Culture</h2>\n'

                               "<p>Humanity's unprecedented set of "
                               'intellectual skills were a key factor in the '
                               "species' eventual technological advancement "
                               'and concomitant domination of the '
                               'biosphere.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-348">[345]</a></sup> '
                               'Disregarding extinct hominids, humans are the '
                               'only animals known to teach generalizable '
                               'information,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-349">[346]</a></sup> '
                               'innately deploy recursive <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dependent_clause">embedding</a> '
                               'to generate and communicate complex '
                               'concepts,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-350">[347]</a></sup> '
                               'engage in the &quot;<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Folk_physics">folk '
                               'physics</a>&quot; required for competent tool '
                               'design,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-351">[348]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-352">[349]</a></sup> '
                               'or cook food in the wild.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-353">[350]</a></sup> '
                               'Teaching and learning preserves the cultural '
                               'and ethnographic identity of human '
                               'societies.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-354">[351]</a></sup> '
                               'Other traits and behaviors that are mostly '
                               'unique to humans include starting '

                               '<a '

                               'structuring<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-356">[353]</a></sup> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vocal_learning">vocal '
                               'learning</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-357">[354]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h3>Language</h3>\n'
                               '<p>Main article: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Language">Language</a></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Primary_Human_Languages_Improved_Version.png"><img '
                               'data-file-height="740" data-file-width="1880" '
                               'src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Primary_Human_Languages_Improved_Version.png/660px-Primary_Human_Languages_Improved_Version.png" '
                               'srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Primary_Human_Languages_Improved_Version.png/495px-Primary_Human_Languages_Improved_Version.png '
                               '1.5x, '
                               '//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Primary_Human_Languages_Improved_Version.png/660px-Primary_Human_Languages_Improved_Version.png '
                               '2x"></img></a><figcaption>Principal <a '
