                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_language_families">language '
                               'families</a> of the world (and in some cases '
                               'geographic groups of families). For greater '
                               'detail, see <i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Template:Distribution_of_languages_in_the_world">Distribution '
                               'of languages in the '
                               'world</a></i>.</figcaption></figure>\n'
                               '<p>While many species <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animal_communication">communicate</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Language">language</a> '
                               'is unique to humans, a defining feature of '
                               'humanity, and a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_universal">cultural '
                               'universal</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-358">[355]</a></sup> '
                               'Unlike the limited systems of other animals, '
                               'human language is open &ndash; an infinite '
                               'number of meanings can be produced by '
                               'combining a limited number of symbols.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-359">[356]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-360">[357]</a></sup> '
                               'Human language also has the capacity of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Displacement_(linguistics)">displacement</a>, '
                               'using words to represent things and happenings '
                               'that are not presently or locally occurring '
                               'but reside in the shared imagination of '
                               'interlocutors.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Revolution-152">[150]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Language differs from other forms of '
                               'communication in that it is <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Origin_of_speech#Modality-independence">modality '
                               'independent</a>; the same meanings can be '
                               'conveyed through different media, audibly in '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speech">speech</a>, '
                               'visually by <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sign_language">sign '
                               'language</a> or writing, and through tactile '
                               'media such as <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille">braille</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-361">[358]</a></sup> '
                               'Language is central to the communication '
                               'between humans, and to the sense of identity '
                               'that unites nations, cultures and ethnic '
                               'groups.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-362">[359]</a></sup> '
                               'There are approximately six thousand different '
                               'languages currently in use, including sign '
                               'languages, and many thousands more that are <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extinct_language">extinct</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-363">[360]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h3>The arts</h3>\n'
                               '<p>Main article: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_arts">The '
                               'arts</a></p>\n'
                               '<p>Human arts can take many forms including <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visual_arts">visual</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literary_arts">literary</a>, '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Performing_arts">performing</a>. '
                               'Visual art can range from <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Painting">paintings</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sculpture">sculptures</a> '
                               'to <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Film">film</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fashion_design">fashion '
                               'design</a>, and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Architecture">architecture</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-364">[361]</a></sup> '
                               'Literary arts can include <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prose">prose</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poetry">poetry</a>, '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drama">dramas</a>. '
                               'The performing arts generally involve <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theatre">theatre</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Music">music</a>, '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dance">dance</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-365">[362]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-366">[363]</a></sup> '
                               'Humans often combine the different forms (for '
                               'example, music videos).<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-367">[364]</a></sup> '
                               'Other entities that have been described as '
                               'having artistic qualities include <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culinary_arts">food '
                               'preparation</a>, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Video_games_as_an_art_form">video '
                               'games</a>, and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medicine">medicine</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-368">[365]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-369">[366]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-370">[367]</a></sup> '
                               'As well as providing entertainment and '
                               'transferring knowledge, the arts are also used '
                               'for <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_arts_and_politics">political '
                               'purposes</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-371">[368]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:British_Museum_Flood_Tablet.jpg"><img '
                               'data-file-height="1137" data-file-width="1005" '
                               'src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/British_Museum_Flood_Tablet.jpg/340px-British_Museum_Flood_Tablet.jpg" '
                               'srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/British_Museum_Flood_Tablet.jpg/255px-British_Museum_Flood_Tablet.jpg '
                               '1.5x, '
                               '//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/British_Museum_Flood_Tablet.jpg/340px-British_Museum_Flood_Tablet.jpg '
                               '2x"></img></a><figcaption>The <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deluge_(mythology)">Deluge</a> '
                               'tablet of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epic_of_Gilgamesh">the '
                               '<i>Gilgamesh</i> epic</a> in <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Akkadian_language">Akkadian</a></figcaption></figure>\n'
                               '<p><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Art">Art</a> '
                               'is a defining characteristic of humans and '
                               'there is evidence for a relationship between '
                               'creativity and language.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Morriss-Kay-2010-372">[369]</a></sup> '
                               'The earliest evidence of art was shell '
                               'engravings made by <i>Homo erectus</i> 300,000 '
                               'years before modern humans evolved.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-373">[370]</a></sup> '
                               'Art attributed to <i>H. sapiens</i> existed at '
                               'least 75,000 years ago, with jewellery and '
                               'drawings found in caves in South '
                               'Africa.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-374">[371]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-375">[372]</a></sup> '
                               'There are various hypotheses as to why humans '
                               'have <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adaptation">adapted</a> '
                               'to the arts. These include allowing them to '
                               'better problem solve issues, providing a means '
                               'to control or influence other humans, '
                               'encouraging cooperation and contribution '
                               'within a society or increasing the chance of '
                               'attracting a potential mate.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-376">[373]</a></sup> '
                               'The use of imagination developed through art, '
                               'combined with logic may have given early '
                               'humans an evolutionary advantage.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Morriss-Kay-2010-372">[369]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Evidence of humans engaging in musical '
                               'activities predates cave art and so far music '
                               'has been <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_universal">practiced '
                               'by virtually all known human '
                               'cultures</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Morley-2014-377">[374]</a></sup> '
                               'There exists a wide variety of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Music_genre">music '
                               'genres</a> and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_music">ethnic '
                               "musics</a>; with humans' musical abilities "
                               'being related to other abilities, including '
                               'complex social human behaviours.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Morley-2014-377">[374]</a></sup> '
                               'It has been shown that human brains respond to '
                               'music by becoming synchronized with the rhythm '
                               'and beat, a process called <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Entrainment_(biomusicology)">entrainment</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-378">[375]</a></sup> '
                               'Dance is also a form of human expression found '
                               'in all cultures<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-379">[376]</a></sup> '
                               'and may have evolved as a way to help early '
                               'humans communicate.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-380">[377]</a></sup> '
                               'Listening to music and observing dance '
                               'stimulates the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orbitofrontal_cortex">orbitofrontal '
                               'cortex</a> and other pleasure sensing areas of '
                               'the brain.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-381">[378]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Unlike speaking, reading and writing does '
                               'not come naturally to humans and must be '
                               'taught.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-382">[379]</a></sup> '
                               'Still, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literature">literature</a> '
                               'has been present before the invention of words '
                               'and language, with 30,000-year-old paintings '
                               'on walls inside some caves portraying a series '
                               'of dramatic scenes.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Puchner-383">[380]</a></sup> '
                               'One of the oldest surviving works of '
                               'literature is the <i><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epic_of_Gilgamesh">Epic '
                               'of Gilgamesh</a></i>, first engraved on '
                               'ancient <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Babylonia">Babylonian</a> '
                               'tablets about 4,000 years ago.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-384">[381]</a></sup> '
                               'Beyond simply passing down knowledge, the use '
                               'and sharing of imaginative <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fiction">fiction</a> '
                               'through stories might have helped develop '
                               "humans' capabilities for communication and "
                               'increased the likelihood of securing a '
                               'mate.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-385">[382]</a></sup> '
                               'Storytelling may also be used as a way to '
                               'provide the audience with moral lessons and '
                               'encourage cooperation.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Puchner-383">[380]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h3>Tools and technologies</h3>\n'
                               '<p>Main articles: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tool">Tool</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technology">Technology</a></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:JR-Maglev-MLX01-2.jpg"><img '
                               'alt="Train running on a track" '
                               'data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" '
                               'src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/JR-Maglev-MLX01-2.jpg/440px-JR-Maglev-MLX01-2.jpg" '
                               'srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/JR-Maglev-MLX01-2.jpg/330px-JR-Maglev-MLX01-2.jpg '
                               '1.5x, '
                               '//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/JR-Maglev-MLX01-2.jpg/440px-JR-Maglev-MLX01-2.jpg '
                               '2x"></img></a><figcaption>The <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SCMaglev">SCMaglev</a>, '
                               'the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_speed_record_for_rail_vehicles">fastest '
                               'train</a> in the world clocking in at 603 km/h '
                               '(375 mph) as of 2015<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-386">[383]</a></sup></figcaption></figure>\n'
                               '<p>Stone tools were used by proto-humans at '
                               'least 2.5 million years ago.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-387">[384]</a></sup> '
                               'The use and manufacture of tools has been put '
                               'forward as the ability that defines humans '
                               'more than anything else<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Choi-2009-388">[385]</a></sup> '
                               'and has historically been seen as an important '
                               'evolutionary step.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-389">[386]</a></sup> '
                               'The technology became much more sophisticated '
                               'about 1.8 million years ago,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Choi-2009-388">[385]</a></sup> '
                               'with the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_of_fire_by_early_humans">controlled '
                               'use of fire</a> beginning around 1 million '
                               'years ago.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-390">[387]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-391">[388]</a></sup> '
                               'The wheel and wheeled vehicles appeared '
                               'simultaneously in several regions some time in '
                               'the fourth millennium BC.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bodnár-2018-68">[68]</a></sup> '
                               'The development of more complex tools and '
                               'technologies allowed land to be <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arable_land">cultivated</a> '
                               'and animals to be <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domestication">domesticated</a>, '
                               'thus proving essential in the development of '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agriculture">agriculture</a> '
                               '&ndash; what is known as the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution">Neolithic '
                               'Revolution</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-392">[389]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>China developed <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paper">paper</a>, '
                               'the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Printing_press">printing '
                               'press</a>, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gunpowder">gunpowder</a>, '
                               'the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compass">compass</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Chinese_inventions">other '
                               'important inventions</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-393">[390]</a></sup> '
                               'The continued improvements in <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smelting">smelting</a> '
                               'allowed <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forging">forging</a> '
                               'of copper, bronze, iron and eventually <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steel">steel</a>, '
                               'which is used in <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Railways">railways</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Skyscraper">skyscrapers</a> '
                               'and many other products.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-394">[391]</a></sup> '
                               'This coincided with the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrial_Revolution">Industrial '
                               'Revolution</a>, where the invention of '
                               'automated machines brought major changes to '
                               "humans' lifestyles.<sup><a "
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-395">[392]</a></sup> '
                               'Modern technology is observed as <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Accelerating_change">progressing '
                               'exponentially</a>,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-396">[393]</a></sup> '
                               'with major innovations in the 20th century '
                               'including: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electricity_generation">electricity</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Penicillin">penicillin</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semiconductor">semiconductors</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine">internal '
                               'combustion engines</a>, the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet">Internet</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fertilizer">nitrogen '
                               'fixing fertilizers</a>, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airplane">airplanes</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer">computers</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Car">automobiles</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Combined_oral_contraceptive_pill">contraceptive '
                               'pills</a>, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_fission">nuclear '
                               'fission</a>, the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_Revolution">green '
                               'revolution</a>, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio">radio</a>, '
                               'scientific <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plant_breeding">plant '
                               'breeding</a>, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rocket">rockets</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Air_conditioning">air '
                               'conditioning</a>, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Television">television</a> '
                               'and the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assembly_line">assembly '
                               'line</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-397">[394]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h3>Religion and spirituality</h3>\n'
                               '<p>Main articles: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion">Religion</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spirituality">Spirituality</a></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Museum_1992.133.4_Figure_of_Shango_on_Horseback.jpg"><img '
                               'data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="1152" '
                               'src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Brooklyn_Museum_1992.133.4_Figure_of_Shango_on_Horseback.jpg/340px-Brooklyn_Museum_1992.133.4_Figure_of_Shango_on_Horseback.jpg" '
                               'srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Brooklyn_Museum_1992.133.4_Figure_of_Shango_on_Horseback.jpg/255px-Brooklyn_Museum_1992.133.4_Figure_of_Shango_on_Horseback.jpg '
                               '1.5x, '
                               '//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Brooklyn_Museum_1992.133.4_Figure_of_Shango_on_Horseback.jpg/340px-Brooklyn_Museum_1992.133.4_Figure_of_Shango_on_Horseback.jpg '
                               '2x"></img></a><figcaption><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shango">Shango</a>, '
                               'the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orisha">Orisha</a> '
                               'of fire, lightning, and thunder, in the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yoruba_religion">Yoruba '
                               'religion</a>, depicted on '
                               'horseback</figcaption></figure>\n'
                               '<p><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Definition_of_religion">Definitions '
                               'of religion</a> vary;<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Idinopulos-1998-398">[395]</a></sup> '
                               'according to one definition, a religion is a '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belief">belief</a> '
                               'system concerning the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supernatural">supernatural</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacred">sacred</a> '
                               'or <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Divinity">divine</a>, '
                               'and practices, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Values">values</a>, '
                               'institutions and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ritual">rituals</a> '
                               'associated with such belief. Some religions '
                               'also have a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moral_code">moral '
                               'code</a>. The <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_psychology_of_religion">evolution</a> '
                               'and the history of the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_origin_of_religions">first '
                               'religions</a> have become areas of active '
                               'scientific investigation.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-399">[396]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-400">[397]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-401">[398]</a></sup> '
                               'Credible evidence of religious behaviour dates '
                               'to the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Paleolithic">Middle '
                               'Paleolithic</a> era (45&ndash;200 <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tya_(unit)">thousand '
                               'years ago</a>).<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-402">[399]</a></sup> '
                               'It may have evolved to play a role in helping '
                               'enforce and encourage cooperation between '
                               'humans.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-403">[400]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Religion manifests in diverse forms.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Idinopulos-1998-398">[395]</a></sup> '
                               'Religion can include a belief in <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life_after_death">life '
                               'after death</a>,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-404">[401]</a></sup> '
                               'the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Origin_of_life">origin '
                               'of life</a>, the nature of the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universe">universe</a> '
                               '(<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religious_cosmology">religious '
                               'cosmology</a>) and its <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultimate_fate">ultimate '
                               'fate</a> (<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eschatology">eschatology</a>), '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morality">moral</a> '
                               'or <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religious_ethics">ethical '
                               'teachings</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-405">[402]</a></sup> '
                               'Views on <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transcendence_(religion)">transcendence</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immanence">immanence</a> '
                               'vary substantially; traditions variously '
                               'espouse <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monism">monism</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deism">deism</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pantheism">pantheism</a>, '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theism">theism</a> '
                               '(including <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polytheism">polytheism</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monotheism">monotheism</a>).<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-406">[403]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Although measuring religiosity is '
                               'difficult,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-407">[404]</a></sup> '
                               'a majority of humans profess some variety of '
                               'religious or spiritual belief.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-408">[405]</a></sup> '
                               'In 2015 the plurality were <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christians">Christian</a> '
                               'followed by <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslims">Muslims</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindus">Hindus</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhism">Buddhists</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-409">[406]</a></sup> '
                               'As of 2015, about 16%, or slightly under 1.2 '
                               'billion humans, were <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irreligious">irreligious</a>, '
                               'including those with no religious beliefs or '
                               'no identity with any religion.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-410">[407]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h3>Science and philosophy</h3>\n'
                               '<p>Main articles: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science">Science</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophy">Philosophy</a></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Dunhuang_star_map.jpg"><img '
                               'data-file-height="2136" data-file-width="2128" '
                               'src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Dunhuang_star_map.jpg/440px-Dunhuang_star_map.jpg" '
                               'srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Dunhuang_star_map.jpg/330px-Dunhuang_star_map.jpg '
                               '1.5x, '
                               '//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Dunhuang_star_map.jpg/440px-Dunhuang_star_map.jpg '
                               '2x"></img></a><figcaption>The <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dunhuang_map">Dunhuang '
                               'map</a>, a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_map">star '
                               'map</a> showing the North Polar region. China '
                               'circa 700.</figcaption></figure>\n'
                               '<p>An aspect unique to humans is their ability '
                               'to <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_transfer">transmit '
                               'knowledge</a> from one generation to the next '
                               'and to continually build on this information '
                               'to develop tools, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_law">scientific '
                               'laws</a> and other advances to pass on '
                               'further.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-411">[408]</a></sup> '
                               'This accumulated knowledge can be tested to '
                               'answer questions or make predictions about how '
                               'the universe functions and has been very '
                               'successful in advancing human '
                               'ascendancy.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-412">[409]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aristotle">Aristotle</a> '
                               'has been described as the first '
                               'scientist,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-413">[410]</a></sup> '
                               'and preceded the rise of scientific thought '
                               'through the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hellenistic_period">Hellenistic '
                               'period</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-414">[411]</a></sup> '
                               'Other early advances in science came from the '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science_and_technology_of_the_Han_dynasty">Han '
                               'dynasty</a> in China and during the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age">Islamic '
                               'Golden Age</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-415">[412]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Renima-2016-94">[94]</a></sup> '
                               'The <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_Revolution">scientific '
                               'revolution</a>, near the end of the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renaissance">Renaissance</a>, '
                               'led to the emergence of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_science">modern '
                               'science</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-416">[413]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>A chain of events and influences led to the '
                               'development of the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_method">scientific '
                               'method</a>, a process of observation and '
                               'experimentation that is used to differentiate '
                               'science from <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pseudoscience">pseudoscience</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-417">[414]</a></sup> '
                               'An understanding of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a> '
                               'is unique to humans, although other species of '
                               'animals have some <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numerical_cognition">numerical '
                               'cognition</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-418">[415]</a></sup> '
                               'All of science can be divided into three major '
                               'branches, the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_sciences">formal '
                               'sciences</a> (e.g., <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic">logic</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>), '
                               'which are concerned with <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_systems">formal '
                               'systems</a>, the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Applied_sciences">applied '
                               'sciences</a> (e.g., engineering, medicine), '
                               'which are focused on practical applications, '
                               'and the empirical sciences, which are based on '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empirical_observation">empirical '
                               'observation</a> and are in turn divided into '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_sciences">natural '
                               'sciences</a> (e.g., <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physics">physics</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemistry">chemistry</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biology">biology</a>) '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_sciences">social '
                               'sciences</a> (e.g., <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psychology">psychology</a>, '
                               'economics, sociology).<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-419">[416]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Philosophy is a field of study where humans '
                               'seek to understand fundamental truths about '
                               'themselves and the world in which they '
                               'live.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-420">[417]</a></sup> '
                               'Philosophical inquiry has been a major feature '
                               "in the development of humans' intellectual "
                               'history.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-421">[418]</a></sup> '
                               "It has been described as the &quot;no man's "
                               'land&quot; between definitive scientific '
                               'knowledge and dogmatic religious '
                               'teachings.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-422">[419]</a></sup> '
                               'Major fields of philosophy include <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metaphysics">metaphysics</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epistemology">epistemology</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic_(philosophy)">logic</a>, '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axiology">axiology</a> '
                               '(which includes <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethics">ethics</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aesthetics">aesthetics</a>).<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-423">[420]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h2>Society</h2>\n'
                               '<p>Main article: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Society">Society</a></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Indian_family_in_Brazil_posed_in_front_of_hut.jpg"><img '
                               'data-file-height="1487" data-file-width="1171" '
                               'src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Indian_family_in_Brazil_posed_in_front_of_hut.jpg/340px-Indian_family_in_Brazil_posed_in_front_of_hut.jpg" '
                               'srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Indian_family_in_Brazil_posed_in_front_of_hut.jpg/255px-Indian_family_in_Brazil_posed_in_front_of_hut.jpg '
                               '1.5x, '
                               '//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Indian_family_in_Brazil_posed_in_front_of_hut.jpg/340px-Indian_family_in_Brazil_posed_in_front_of_hut.jpg '
                               '2x"></img></a><figcaption>Humans often live in '
                               'family-based social '
                               'structures.</figcaption></figure>\n'
                               '<p>Society is the system of organizations and '
                               'institutions arising from interaction between '
                               'humans. Humans are highly social and tend to '
                               'live in large complex social groups. They can '
                               'be divided into different groups according to '
                               'their income, wealth, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Power_(social_and_political)">power</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reputation">reputation</a> '
                               'and other factors. The structure of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_stratification">social '
                               'stratification</a> and the degree of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_mobility">social '
                               'mobility</a> differs, especially between '
                               'modern and traditional societies.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-424">[421]</a></sup> '
                               'Human groups range from the size of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Family">families</a> '
                               'to nations. The first form of human social '
                               'organization is thought to have resembled <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherer</a> '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Band_society">band '
                               'societies</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-425">[422]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h3>Gender</h3>\n'
                               '<p>Main article: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gender">Gender</a></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Human.svg"><img '
                               'data-file-height="1320" data-file-width="1060" '
                               'src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Human.svg/340px-Human.svg.png" '
                               'srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Human.svg/255px-Human.svg.png '
                               '1.5x, '
                               '//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Human.svg/340px-Human.svg.png '
                               '2x"></img></a><figcaption>Depiction of a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Man">man</a> '
                               'and a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Woman">woman</a> '
                               'from the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pioneer_plaque">Pioneer '
                               'plaque</a></figcaption></figure>\n'
                               '<p>Human societies typically exhibit <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gender_identity">gender '
                               'identities</a> and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gender_role">gender '
                               'roles</a> that distinguish between <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masculinity">masculine</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Femininity">feminine</a> '
                               'characteristics and prescribe the range of '
                               'acceptable behaviours and attitudes for their '
                               'members based on their <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sex">sex</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-426">[423]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-427">[424]</a></sup> '
                               'The most common categorisation is a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gender_binary">gender '
                               'binary</a> of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Men">men</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women">women</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-428">[425]</a></sup> '
                               'Some societies recognize a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_gender">third '
                               'gender</a>,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-429">[426]</a></sup> '
                               'or less commonly a fourth or fifth.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-430">[427]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-431">[428]</a></sup> '
                               'In some other societies, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-binary_gender">non-binary</a> '
                               'is used as an umbrella term for a range of '
                               'gender identities that are not solely male or '
                               'female.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-432">[429]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Gender roles are often associated with a '
                               'division of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_norm">norms</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Practice_(social_theory)">practices</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clothing">dress</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_behavior">behavior</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rights">rights</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duty">duties</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Privilege_(social_inequality)">privileges</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_status">status</a>, '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Power_(social_and_political)">power</a>, '
                               'with men enjoying more rights and privileges '
                               'than women in most societies, both today and '
                               'in the past.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-433">[430]</a></sup> '
                               'As a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_constructionism">social '
                               'construct</a>,<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-434">[431]</a></sup> '
                               'gender roles are not fixed and vary '
                               'historically within a society. Challenges to '
                               'predominant gender norms have recurred in many '
                               'societies.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-435">[432]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-436">[433]</a></sup> '
                               'Little is known about gender roles in the '
                               'earliest human societies. <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_modern_human">Early '
                               'modern humans</a> probably had a range of '
                               'gender roles similar to that of modern '
                               'cultures from at least the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upper_Paleolithic">Upper '
                               'Paleolithic</a>, while the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neanderthal">Neanderthals</a> '
                               'were less sexually dimorphic and there is '
                               'evidence that the behavioural difference '
                               'between males and females was minimal.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-437">[434]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h3>Kinship</h3>\n'
                               '<p>Main article: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kinship">Kinship</a></p>\n'
                               '<p>All human societies organize, recognize and '
                               'classify types of social relationships based '
                               'on relations between parents, children and '
                               'other descendants (<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consanguinity">consanguinity</a>), '
                               'and relations through <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marriage">marriage</a> '
                               '(<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Affinity_(law)">affinity</a>). '
                               'There is also a third type applied to <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Godparent">godparents</a> '
                               'or <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adoption">adoptive '
                               'children</a> (<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fictive_kinship">fictive</a>). '
                               'These culturally defined relationships are '
                               'referred to as kinship. In many societies, it '
                               'is one of the most important social organizing '
                               'principles and plays a role in transmitting '
                               'status and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inheritance">inheritance</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-438">[435]</a></sup> '
                               'All societies have rules of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Incest_taboo">incest '
                               'taboo</a>, according to which marriage between '
                               'certain kinds of kin relations is prohibited, '
                               'and some also have rules of preferential '
                               'marriage with certain kin relations.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-439">[436]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Pair bonding is a ubiquitous feature of '
                               'human sexual relationships, whether it is '
                               'manifested as serial monogamy, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polygyny">polygyny</a>, '
                               'or <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polyandry">polyandry</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-440">[437]</a></sup> '
                               'Genetic evidence indicates that humans were '
                               'predominantly <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polygyny">polygynous</a> '
                               'for most of their existence as a species, but '
                               'that this began to shift during the Neolithic, '
                               'when <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monogamy">monogamy</a> '
                               'started becoming widespread concomitantly with '
                               'the transition from nomadic to sedentary '
                               'societies.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-441">[438]</a></sup> '
                               'Anatomical evidence in the form of '
                               'second-to-fourth digit ratios, a biomarker for '
                               'prenatal androgen effects, likewise indicates '
                               'modern humans were polygynous during the '
                               'Pleistocene.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-442">[439]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h3>Ethnicity</h3>\n'
                               '<p>Main article: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_group">Ethnic '
                               'group</a></p>\n'
                               '<p>Human ethnic groups are a social category '
                               'that <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Identity_(social_science)">identifies</a> '
                               'together as a group based on shared attributes '
                               'that distinguish them from other groups. These '
                               'can be a common set of traditions, <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancestry">ancestry</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Language">language</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History">history</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Society">society</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture">culture</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nation">nation</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion">religion</a>, '
                               'or social treatment within their residing '
                               'area.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-443">[440]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-444">[441]</a></sup> '
                               'Ethnicity is separate from the concept of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Race_(human_categorization)">race</a>, '
                               'which is based on physical characteristics, '
                               'although both are <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_constructionism">socially '
                               'constructed</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-445">[442]</a></sup> '
                               'Assigning ethnicity to a certain population is '
                               'complicated, as even within common ethnic '
                               'designations there can be a diverse range of '
                               'subgroups, and the makeup of these ethnic '
                               'groups can change over time at both the '
                               'collective and individual level.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-REGWG2005-178">[176]</a></sup> '
                               'Also, there is no generally accepted '
                               'definition of what constitutes an ethnic '
                               'group.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-446">[443]</a></sup> '
                               'Ethnic groupings can play a powerful role in '
                               'the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_identity">social '
                               'identity</a> and solidarity of ethnopolitical '
                               'units. This has been closely tied to the rise '
                               'of the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nation_state">nation '
                               'state</a> as the predominant form of political '
                               'organization in the 19th and 20th '
                               'centuries.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-447">[444]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-448">[445]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-449">[446]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h3>Government and politics</h3>\n'
                               '<p>Main articles: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government">Government</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politics">Politics</a></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City,_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg"><img '
                               'data-file-height="1611" data-file-width="3144" '
                               'src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City%2C_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg/440px-United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City%2C_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg" '
                               'srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City%2C_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg/330px-United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City%2C_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg '
                               '1.5x, '
                               '//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City%2C_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg/440px-United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City%2C_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg '
                               '2x"></img></a><figcaption>The <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Headquarters_of_the_United_Nations">United '
                               'Nations headquarters</a> (left) in New York '
                               "City, which houses one of the world's largest "
                               'political organizations</figcaption></figure>\n'
                               '<p>As farming populations gathered in larger '
                               'and denser communities, interactions between '
                               'these different groups increased. This led to '
                               'the development of governance within and '
                               'between the communities.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-450">[447]</a></sup> '
                               'Humans have evolved the ability to change '
                               'affiliation with various social groups '
                               'relatively easily, including previously strong '
                               'political alliances, if doing so is seen as '
                               'providing personal advantages.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-451">[448]</a></sup> '
                               'This <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_flexibility">cognitive '
                               'flexibility</a> allows individual humans to '
                               'change their political ideologies, with those '
                               'with higher flexibility less likely to support '
                               'authoritarian and nationalistic '
                               'stances.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-452">[449]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Governments create <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law">laws</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Policies">policies</a> '
                               'that affect the citizens that they govern. '
                               'There have been <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_forms_of_government">many '
                               'forms of government</a> throughout human '
                               'history, each having various means of '
                               'obtaining power and the ability to exert '
                               'diverse controls on the population.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-453">[450]</a></sup> '
                               'Approximately 47% of humans live in some form '
                               'of a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democracy">democracy</a>, '
                               '17% in a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hybrid_regime">hybrid '
                               'regime</a>, and 37% in an <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_regime">authoritarian '
                               'regime</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-454">[451]</a></sup> '
                               'Many countries belong to <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_organization">international '
                               'organizations</a> and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alliances">alliances</a>; '
                               'the largest of these is the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations">United '
                               'Nations</a>, with <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations">193 '
                               'member states</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-455">[452]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h3>Trade and economics</h3>\n'
                               '<p>Main articles: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trade">Trade</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economics">Economics</a></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Silk_route.jpg"><img '
                               'data-file-height="1866" data-file-width="2868" '
                               'src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Silk_route.jpg/580px-Silk_route.jpg" '
                               'srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Silk_route.jpg/435px-Silk_route.jpg '
                               '1.5x, '
                               '//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Silk_route.jpg/580px-Silk_route.jpg '
                               '2x"></img></a><figcaption>The <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silk_Road">Silk '
                               'Road</a> (red) and spice <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trade_routes">trade '
                               'routes</a> (blue)</figcaption></figure>\n'
                               '<p>Trade, the voluntary exchange of goods and '
                               'services, is seen as a characteristic that '
                               'differentiates humans from other animals and '
                               'has been cited as a practice that gave <i>Homo '
                               'sapiens</i> a major advantage over other '
                               'hominids.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-456">[453]</a></sup> '
                               'Evidence suggests early <i>H. sapiens</i> made '
                               'use of long-distance trade routes to exchange '
                               'goods and ideas, leading to <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_explosion">cultural '
                               'explosions</a> and providing additional food '
                               'sources when hunting was sparse, while such '
                               'trade networks did not exist for the now '
                               'extinct Neanderthals.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-457">[454]</a></sup><sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-458">[455]</a></sup> '
                               'Early trade likely involved materials for '
                               'creating tools like <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Obsidian">obsidian</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-459">[456]</a></sup> '
                               'The first truly international trade routes '
                               'were around the <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spice_trade">spice '
                               'trade</a> through the Roman and medieval '
                               'periods.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-460">[457]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<p>Early human <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy">economies</a> '
                               'were more likely to be based around <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gift_economy">gift '
                               'giving</a> instead of a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barter">bartering</a> '
                               'system.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-461">[458]</a></sup> '
                               'Early <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Money">money</a> '
                               'consisted of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commodity_money">commodities</a>; '
                               'the oldest being in the form of cattle and the '
                               'most widely used being <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cowrie_shells">cowrie '
                               'shells</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-www.pbs.org-1996-462">[459]</a></sup> '
                               'Money has since evolved into governmental '
                               'issued <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coins">coins</a>, '
                               '<a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paper_money">paper</a> '
                               'and <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electronic_money">electronic '
                               'money</a>.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-www.pbs.org-1996-462">[459]</a></sup> '
                               'Human study of economics is a <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_science">social '
                               'science</a> that looks at how societies '
                               'distribute scarce resources among different '
                               'people.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-463">[460]</a></sup> '
                               'There are massive <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_inequality">inequalities</a> '
                               'in the division of <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wealth">wealth</a> '
                               'among humans; the eight richest humans are '
                               'worth the same monetary value as the poorest '
                               'half of all the human population.<sup><a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-464">[461]</a></sup></p>\n'
                               '<h3>Conflict</h3>\n'
                               '<p>Main article: <a '
                               'href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conflict_(process)">Conflict '
                               '(process)</a></p>\n'
                               '<figure><a '
